Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	There is one method for this where you make III cauteries, or IV, by tracing according to the length of the mouse, according to the shape of the cautery that we have described before; and do not press your hand at all along the cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; and another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery with II nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the part where the mouse is, or the armpit from which the disease comes towards the left, and the elevation by which you lift the part according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After that, put the II nerves in flame until the heart is pierced from the other side; then draw away the cautery, and thus it will have IV. And if you wish, cauterize throughout the cautery with III nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the scrofula has been treated for a long time, and it does not heal as quickly as the other diseases mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not effective for dropsy, except in the manner that is called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in divisions, and your treatment is not effective, then you should perform four cauterizations around the armpit, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the abdomen, two in the back on the spine, and one at the tailbone; the cautery should be close to the thick part of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After leaving the cautery open to draw pus for a long time, do not leave the cure of the patient after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is the chisel that we have previously shown; and for the back it should be olive-shaped, according to what has been described earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet of the dropsical person are swollen and filled with yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring finger; then lift your hand with the cautery without turning.Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, thus it would press against the yellow awl, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, make 2 cauteries on each leg at the top of the tibia; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other above, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries to heal without bandaging, until the water comes out; then dress the others as we have said.
de la menoison	of the brain
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When diarrhea comes from coldness and moisture, when the retentive and digestive faculties in the stomach and intestines are impaired, and cannot be cured by means of remedies; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with much strength, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before regarding the cautery of the stomach, with the circulating cautery; and four small cauteries around the belly, each cautery being subtle, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the elbow, and one cautery on each shoulder joint, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good support.Et si li fai  .i. cautere sus la tete, et  .i. cautere de costé, et  .ij. cauteres entor la cheville subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil; car li cure est profitans a ceus qui sont desaloiez de lor leu.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure for hemorrhoidsAnd si li fai   .i . cautere sus la tete , et  .i . cautere de costé , et  .ij . cauteres entor la cheville subtilz a tout  .i . cautere clavile subtil ; car li cure est profitans a ceus qui sont desaloiez de lor leu .de la cure des emorroydes
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and are old and filled with cold, moist, corrupted humors, and they are cured as we have described through divisions, but it does not help, then do cautery: three times on the spine of the back, that which is completely outside below the armpit, little by little in a triangular shape; and do cautery under the jaw, twice; and if you think the stomach is cold, and the meat is not digested, and they see swelling in the face, then on the face do one large cautery on the stomach, as it is described before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse with the full cautery of a clavicle; and let the cautery remain open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After curing the site until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshiness which is named "thelul."
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you scrape the "thelul", heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it fully heated on the scraped "thelul"; and hold your hand so that the cauteries reach the source of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; afterward treat them with healing ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the scrotum, it will be of greater aid.
de plaie mal curee	of poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is a fistula and it is suppurating and exuding pus and corrupted moisture, then you should probe it with a thin rod and be careful that you know how deep the rod goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery iron until it is red hot, insert it into the fistula according to the depth of the rod that went in, and repeat the cautery until the pus and corruption are burned, once or twice or three times, depending on how much is needed; be careful not to burn any nerves that might be nearby, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	if the fistula goes into the bladder and intestines, be careful with these areas, and do not apply the cautery too strongly, and think that it is not healed; after the site is healed and if the opening is still there and the matter is not discharged for a long time, then know that the site is completely healed; and if the matter is not discharged, know that the site is punctured and the bone at the bottom is damaged; and thus as one of those we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain comes with rain and strong winds, and takes hold of a woman, then you must make a cautery on the rains on both sides using the key cautery that we mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize it in the middle, there will be three cauteries in a line, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, and the patient retains urine due to the condition, then make a cautery on the part above the bladder where the hairs of the pubic region start, with one cautery on the right and one on the left, and let each cautery be as long as the width of two fingers; also, make one cautery below the back, or two if you need them; and use the key cautery as described earlier.
de la marris	of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the matrix is cold and moist, and does not permit conception, and the flowers are corrupt and their terms late; and when they come, there is great pain: therefore one must make three cauteries around the womb, as we have said in the cautery for the bladder, and two cauteries on the back; and let the cauteries be of a mild nature, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the box of the hip, and because of this they move out of place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when one measures them together; and it is found that the place of the dislocation is hollow, then one must cauterize the patient on the box of the hip with 1 cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the location around the box as it turns, so that the box is within the circle; and let the cautery be like that which one uses to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not present, make three cauteries of the olive oil large, and let the cautery be as deep as all the scabs; and heal it until it is better.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hip socket, it is caused by cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of thick humors with foul-smelling pills, or other good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterward, let him apply a cautery; and there are two ways of applying cauteries: that is to say, with burning drugs, or with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauteries are of many types, one of which is as follows: you should make three triangular cauteries on the hip joint according to this shape, and they should be deep and large, with a space between each cautery the width of a thumb; the cauteries should be olive-shaped. Sometimes, a cautery is made in the center of the hip joint according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you want to cauterize with the circular cauterization that we mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the thickness of the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is how one treats sciatica when the pain stays in the hip and does not go down into the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain extends to one or both sides of the leg or foot, he should be cauterized where he feels the pain in three or four places with what is called the "point cautery." The cautery should be a small needle, and the thickness of the skin should be burnt. If the patient feels that the pain extends all the way to the toe or close to it, then he should be cauterized where he feels the pain in three or four places with what is called the "point cautery.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make more cauteries; and if he feels that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, then use a cutaneous or circular cautery, and be careful with all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several who have had cautery performed on the ankle of the foot, and they left it until the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it was pierced and corrupted all through the foot.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a stomachache that caused his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, perform cautery on both, according to this manner.Et si li dolors est en deux parties ensamble, fais cautere en l'une et en l'auter, selont cette maniere.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said about the cautery of the hip, of which this is the manner, make the iron and let it be at the head as large as a thumb-nail, or a little less, and let it be pierced and let there be between them the distance of two fingers, and they must be on both sides, and they must also be like nuts; and it must have a good handle. And this is its shape:Et li saiges dirent de la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com un nauvillon de dacte ou un poc moins et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetre jusc’a l’auter d’espaice la cantitat d’un nou de poce, et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait li mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is all red and dripping hot, and then place it on the box of the painful hip, and let it be turned onto the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery and leave it for 3 days; and then make a poultice of butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sight, and those who are experienced in it use little; and nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries which can be endured, and it lies where it occurs.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns when you make the instrument to interlock in such a way that the rim of the door descends, and is made of brass or iron with a long surface, and at its height has two notches, and between each one there is the thickness of a fingernail; and are open below and above, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Afterwards, place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his healthy side, and press your hand firmly on the box of the hip; afterwards pour between the two circles of hot vinegar which has been heated in the fire for a moment, and let the patient bear the heat and burning for an hour.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds biting as well as fire; and when the bites have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip with gentle vinegar, and let it be so for three days, and put butter on it until the blackness of the scald is gone; and leave it for three days until pus comes out; and that would be the last aid after the treatment of ointments until he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, you shall make the instrument that colors in accordance with what you have done in the hip joint; and that is the manner of hot ash, and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and quicklime, as much of each, and grind them together, and place them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	And in that pot is a small hole so that the point of a needle can enter; and place on top of that pot another pot well sealed, and place on top of the alkaline and chalk and ash water on top, until it has two fingers above the powders after you have well moistened your hand; and let it be thus until there falls ash and pieces into the sealed pot, then take all that ash, and pour it over the hot chalk and alkaline as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then there will be much fever, and it is administered in the form of medicine and cauteries of other members; for it does as bad a job as fire, and so with other medicines from which one cauterizes the hip well, such as thistle and honey and soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of hip and sciatic pain, and he praised it greatly, saying that nothing else was done to him, and that he was healed at once when this cure was performed, and that he bathed as he instructed below:
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he said in such a way that you take litharge green and dry, and grind it very fine with a little tallow, and apply it to the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and let it sit; and leave it for three hours, and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter the bath until his body is a little warmed up, and let him enter the bed, and the pain will go away completely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medicine after an evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps a lot; and the cautery should be performed in the following way:
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lamb's wool and grease it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the big toe and the one next to it, which is called the sciatic nerve.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat's dung and heat it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the wool, and leave it until the pain is gone; and do this again, and keep doing this until you feel that it has reached the hip and the pain has stopped; and this cautery method is called "goat cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When back pain comes from sitting or impact or from excessive evacuation, or from similar appearances of cold matter, none of these warrant cauterization except that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is appropriate, after the patient has voided foul pills or other similar substances, to make three marks on their back where the pain is located, and in each mark, administer .v. cauteries or more depending on the strength and amount that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be performed according to the cautery called 'point'; and if you see fit, perform .iij or .iiij cauteries with the medium-sized cautery instrument according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often affects young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight, constricted appearance when they wake up, and fear; and you will find it in the last vertebrae of the back and in the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you cure it, then cauterize it with a cautery of salt according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the purple cautery equally affects every part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery tool 2 or 3 lines apart, and have the pricks close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterward, treat the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and beware of administering cautery in areas with gangrene that is in the webbing between fingers or toes.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture that is spread throughout the body's limbs, and when pain comes in the feet, which the doctors properly call 'podagra', and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cauteries in such a way: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick the sole of the foot, do the cautery with the entire tool that is called «point.»
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and that happens many times, do cautery on each knee III or IV cauteries of each part, using the entire olive-shaped tool; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand there any longer than until the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cautery that we have described in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make punctures around the wrist two lines; and if there is no pain remaining in the fingers, make punctures on each joint and on the palm of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good management for the patient and take medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you provide good management for him and purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rot of the eye socket
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the ulcer comes in the anus, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is new, then when you see him being cured, he should not defecate that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the farts descend from his belly; after that, let him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to press his anus until the bowels are repaired, and bring them back to your fingers, and sign with chalk underneath the ulcer on the bone of the buttock, and throughout a sign that is similar to half a circle on top of the body; then heat the cautery from which this form comes:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it becomes white and starts to ooze pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and have the patient hold his hand so that it does not return; and work the thighs well for the patient, and put a pillow and a servant under the thighs, and another under the buttocks to keep the hands from moving; then put the cautery on the wound all over your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the pus does not ooze when you are doing the cautery, so that you do not burn him, and so that the patient does not die or suffer harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to the size of their ears, and for large people as large according to their size; after three days, treat the site of the cautery with butter until the scorch is removed; then treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary to let his hair grow long enough that his head does not get wet when he goes out in the rain.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage which he should wear for another forty days; and let him have good rest, do little work, and guard against too much drinking and eating, and straining his voice too much; and if he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will now describe how to treat an abscess on the head.
de la routure dou ventre	of the bowel movement
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers appear on other parts of the body and are recognized, and you see that they are no longer growing, then treat them with fire cautery according to their size, burning to one third of the skin's depth; after this, treat them as described above. Some ancient writers say that they should be cauterized with a three-pointed cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the site with charcoal and draw a line around the edge of the ulcer, and another from above it, and keep your hand steady while doing all the cauterization.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cautery is lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain occurs in a limb, whether from a fall or injury, and the pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment does not help, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "point," according to the length of the limb, its smallness, weakness, location, and the nature of the pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, do another cautery on top of it, for such is the custom that it should move in the member that is nearest to it, so you must do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	from mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The diseases are sometimes aided by cautery with great benefit, especially those that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see her cauterized, take care whether the disease is in its beginning, and if it is healed according to what we have said in the division, and does not go away or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the whole disease, then do five cauteries on the head: one on the crown at the front of the hair, and one on each temple, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and let your hand remain so that the cautery reaches the bone, and as much as the scalp comes out from it so that the vapors of the gross humors can issue out through it; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the disease is scattered throughout the body, and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize her with these cauteries that we have mentioned on the head, and one cautery in the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the groin and another there, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are on the back of the calf. And sometimes do one cautery on the bone of the arm, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do cauterization, the more it helps, and moves the profit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person does, because the body is already entirely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After that, treat the site with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it does not heal, then you should do cauterization on the member according to its size; and the cautery should be slightly inserted into the depth of the skin; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is performed on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; yet no one should undertake this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	of almond milk
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" appears, and medicine does not help, then cauterize it with a slightly deep cautery, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with a poultice of linseed and lentil flour, with rose oil, and plantain leaves, and colon blood and almond blood, each ingredient being used in equal parts. Mix everything together and apply it, wrapped in a cloth, to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure of cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a ulcer first appears, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a circle, all around the edge of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the ulcer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear it will be burned and corrupted, and I have indeed seen this happen sometimes; and a more certain thing is that it is cauterized around the edge, with a cautery called 'circle', as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot subside
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it lingers, either because of the excess fluid it produces or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, very old), and he has little blood, or due to the duration of the illness; and you see him hastening to die: therefore cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; then leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten death.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all the way through, then heat the cautery with which it is formed:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called  "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the skin, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them drawing out in such a way that the flow of the pus is slowed.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cautery by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of disease which is called   "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a eating away of a limb, for it gnaws at the limbs just as fire burns dry wood.Et adonques covient ke li membres siano defformiez, et li malaides se sentont grant dolor, si com ilo est a la maladie  «adubelati».
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can withstand fire cautery, then heat the cautery iron very small and large, according to what is appropriate for the location of the disease; after cauterizing all over, so that you reach all the corruption, and none remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply soothing ointment to the cauterized areas with oil until the fire wounds are healed, and all the corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Afterward, use healing ointments generated from flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that new flesh is not growing, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.Et s’il aduient que li membres soit demores por cause de moistor ne de froid, si covient qu’on le chauffe avec char pians, et le curee et le chauffe, et le curee, et l’oigne, tant qu’il soit sain, et le laisse III jors.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this disease has sometimes been cured by medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is much more effective, and I have already described the cure for medicine ague in the previous chapter: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that appear on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that a disease called 'ulcer' in our language occurs on the feet due to moisture, and is a large, rotten mass that bleeds from the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the treatment for this disease has two methods:
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	Namely fire cautery and hot water cautery.Et li un prend la chair en haut et la tue et tue li piez; et l’auter ne tuet pas la chair, mes tue li nervues qui sont dedens le piet.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is where you heat the cautery as hot as a needle, and it is made of good iron to the size that it can pierce the nail on all sides, and has thin edges; after which, you apply it hot to the nail and rotate your hand around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; then let it be for three days until pus starts to come out; then make a poultice of crushed mallows with salt, and leave the poultice on overnight, and the nail will fall off and be pulled out by its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with a healing ointment until it is cured.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are turned away from the body, and often occur in hands and feet, then you should administer hot water cautery; and it is in such a way: take a brass or iron rod, or a pen, and place it over the nail and the skin, that is, warts; and place the rod so that it covers all around, then put a little drop of hot water, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep into the root; and let the patient endure the burning sensation of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be pulled out by its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you draw out all those who are in the body, then cure the wounds which generate pus.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever or other, you should make them .iiij. cauteries or .iv. on the spine of the back, .i. cautery between each vertebrae; and .i. cautery on the feet, and .i. on the stomach with an olive-sized cautery; this will stop the shaking and hasten the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes they appear as sores on the body, or foul pustules, which come from corrupted humors.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If necessary, when they first appear, one should make a cautery on each tip of the pustule: with a thin cautery of myrtle wood, whose point is taken up in fire, or of long aristolache root, or with the lens-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, according to this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the surplusage from which they come is disrupted, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.Si ele est si grant que elle soit de la granture d’une fuit ou plus, si faice li cautere sus le chief de la pustule, et non pas sur le corps de la pustule, car il ne faict si granz domages com s’il estoit fait sus li corps.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are many times great bleeding from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or with the incision of an abscess, or with the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very sorrowful thing to stanch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger over the wound of the vein and hold it very tightly until the blood is calmed beneath your finger and no drop comes out; then take several small and large olive-wood cauteries and heat them in the fire until they are all red; then take a little salt, either large or small depending on the wound and where the artery is rupture, and place the cautery over that vein where you hold your finger, and keep it there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds when you lift your finger from the wound and the cauteries are extinguished, quickly take another one of the cauteries which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and beware of damaging the nerve which lies nearby, and that no further harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped well by itself alone if the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have mentioned: either by cautery or extraction when it is not treated, or by a strong ligature, or by medicines placed on which have power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and pressed gently.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers a tight binding of bandages or places burning things on top, or similar things, will not benefit if only a little.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have any medicine available, then they should put their index finger on the wound as we have said, and press firmly both on the wound and the vein; and they should not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and swollen and pressed firm; and they should make inquiries in advance about what cauteries and medicines are needed.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of wound treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all illnesses that require cautery with fire or burning medicines, and their cause, instrument, form of cauteries; and I have placed that chapter from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter by the same path so that one may more easily find what they want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I may begin this, my dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of this greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For there are many ways that people come into care.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come from such who are so worn down by their illness that they die easily because of the wear and tear of their disease, and because of the great severity of their suffering; and one must fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give up their senses and say, "Wait, I am healed"; and the disease is stubborn.Et il doit on avoir paor por ce que il ne se remue pas tant qu’il est garnis de sa cure; car il peut bien avenir que li maladie revienne et li corps soit despitous.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more confidence in your honor than in your desire. Do not open foolishly, but wisely, that of which you are certain and from which you can gain profit and fame. Use prognostication and indication in the cure of your illnesses, to which salvation is turned; and this will aid you in acquiring a good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Lord gives you good understanding and righteousness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter in a discourse on chapters, according to what it is before the chapter on cauteries, which I have discussed from the head to the feet, so that you can find more easily whatever you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to infants during childbirth, and when the birth canal is too narrow for the baby's head; and sometimes it comes from a relaxed birth canal, which no one knows about.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and in all those that I have seen, death soon followed; and for this reason it seems better to me to leave the treatment in a few simple remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was swollen with water, and the swelling increased every day until he could no longer bear it; and he died of the moisture, which had gathered under the skull between the brain and the bone; and if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, then make a large slit in the head, as long as two fingers, so that the moisture may flow out; and here is the form of the spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the corners of the head opening in every part, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it does not close up again: then you must make three slits in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all moisture forcibly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterward, tighten the incisions with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, leaving it for five days. Then remove the bandages and cure the wound by tenting and anointing, allowing the head to hang freely, and feed the patient dry meat to dry up any moisture, until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens, and the gathering of pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess opens and the gathering of pus, and pierce according to what you can; and be careful not to cut the artery, and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	from gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When someone suffers from a condition called "cataract" in the eyes or feet, and the disease is old, and medical treatment is ineffective, then the best course of action is cauterization by cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see them covered, that the patient bends his head backwards; then rub the area around his neck with a rough cloth until the veins appear, then press the patient's neck all the way to the cloth; then look where the vein runs, and its course is from behind the ears, and it is very deep; then mark the spot, then cover both sides with a sharp spatula, as far as the vein, and this should be done through the back of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, put the spatulum under the artery and cut it from above, cutting also as deep as two fingers across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood will flow out continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the vein does not appear to the touch, then you must measure the amount of space between three fingers, then mark and cut to the bone; and the amount of blood that should be let out is six ounces, and by accident a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the filling of the vein. Then examine the wound: if there remains nothing on the bone, cut so that warm pus does not come, then press and bandage the wound with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of emetic
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient emigrant comes, and catarrh is acute, for the moistors of tears and the chills in temples and ancient soddeness and similar things, and it is medicined by manners of cures of medicine and all that does not benefit him at all, then let us draw out the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have related.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the extraction of them is that the patient pulls back the hair of his temples, and feels the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is little relaxed outwards when in some men who are too cold; and if it is relaxed, then the patient strains his neck with some cloth, then rubs the place with some rough cloth, and washes the place with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatulum made from which there is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly scorch the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upward with tweezers, and carefully separate it from the tissue underneath in each part; and if the artery is delicate, return it to the tip of the fingernail, then cover that part according to the amount of the two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not covered, the blood will not stop flowing everywhere.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from 1/4 to 3/8 of an inch; and if the artery is large, you should tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound heals, and bleeding comes slowly; then bandage the excess between the two ties in the same hour, and if you wish, cauterize it with a hot-iron cautery up to the bone so that the shoulder is cut; and this is the best treatment if the patient doesn’t have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	Because cauterization helps to end moisture; that is why it is more helpful for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the place with old cotton and places it on well-made tents; and when they are taken off, cure them with dry medicines that cause pus to form, and with tents, until they are healed; and if there is an artery without a vein as far as you work, hasten to cover by cauterization, or employ vitriol and stretch out your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you don’t have that at hand, put your finger on the place so that the blood congeals, and moisten the place with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as it should be; and what is better and lighter in the extraction of an artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of 2 parts, but let the cutter be well thickened so that its heat lasts longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when an instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less well.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And between the two knives there should be a space of a finger's width, and then when you have cut through both sides and placed the hot iron on as far as the bone, and split the vein in two places; and the two parts should be pulled apart so that they are not fused by this cautery all the way through. This is how the cautery tool should be formed:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.
