When tears are flowing from the eyes which are above the testicles on the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and there is a beating in his forehead as if from trembling; and if the eyelids are thin and moist so that the hairs have fallen out, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the "crushed wound" in the old language, and it is for you to do on the patient who has this disease to let the hairs grow on his forehead, then make III incisions on his forehead evenly according to the length of his forehead; and one of the incisions should be as long as two fingers across his forehead, going down into the eye socket, and the other two on either side above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on either side above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the jaw, and each wound should be the length of three fingers across, joined together; and have ready a piece of sponge and a lot of gauze to soak up the blood, then insert the spatulum into both parts where the deformation is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the skin that is between the two incisions up to the bone, then do likewise from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then remove this spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first incision the instrument that is called  "cultellarius," and it is very sharp on one side, and not at all sharp on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place it cutting towards the chest to the heart, and the flat side towards the bone, and cut until it reaches the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what is open from the heart, and then make another cut in the middle split to the other defiant; and then draw out blood equally, and express the place for the drawn blood; then put a tent made of old cotton into each split, and put wet clothes soaked in wine and oil and garlic on it, and guard against hot abscesses coming to it; and on the third day loosen the ligature, and administer plenty of cold water, then cure it with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other cures used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has a constant catarrh, and you see the eyes are sunken and small, and the vision weakened, and the eyelids burnt, and the hair falling out, and in the head there is pain, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that these matters and this catarrh come from many veins, and the remedy for it is to cure what is inside.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to look straight ahead, then make a large slit in the middle of his forehead, and another one an inch wide.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and cut down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that move when you chew; and once the bone is exposed, wipe away all the blood with a sponge, and then insert old cotton and tenting of linen between the two lips of the incision; then bind wet bandages soaked in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses; when it is healed, you should rub the bone until new tissue starts to grow, then treat it with drying things that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat-flower and four parts of colophony, make an ointment from it, and administer it to promote healing throughout the wound.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains or a beast, or stone from a mine, or similar object like iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, and lentils; or flowing liquid, like water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it sinks into the ear stone or any other foreign object that does not adhere to or grow in the ear, hold the ear towards the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, drop a little violet oil or oil of wormwood on it, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with powdered scent, and plug his nostrils when the sneezing comes on, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and let the ear be uppermost.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	It often comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then one administers extraction with fine forceps, as shown in the figure.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a fine needle of small wire; and if it does not come out in this way, then make an iron hook and insert the tip of the hook into the ear canal firmly, and plug the area around the hook with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out gently, for often it comes out as we have said. And if it does not come out in such a way, then take some glut and use it to grab birds, and place some instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put some cotton around it; then press the glut onto the pebble or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out with all the things we have said, then be quick to split the ear so that pus and blood comes out, and a spasm; and the manner of the splitting is that you first make the patient fast for three days, and bleed him according to his condition, then make him sit between your hands and turn his ear upwards, and make a small slit in the root of the ear at the fat where it depends; and the slit should be like a crescent moon, so that you can reach the pebble, then remove it according to your ability, and suck on it strongly with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is inside and it swells, then administer removal; and if it cannot come out, then administer .i. spatumile with a thin needle according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that spot.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many attempts; then extract it with fine forceps and a suction tube, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.Et si tu ne puets le faire aligerement, et que li piere soit grant et secque, puis le faire secher avec oile de l’arbre d’alosee, et quant il est sec adousé de oile d’olive et de pite, et li sucurses de l’estrainne, si com nos avons dit; et li estraignons la seconde foiz alergeument.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the pain therefore that falls into the ear, the patient should use snuff of first materials, and stuff the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let him lie on that very ear where the pain is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out through the air, that is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not go out through the air, then take many small stones according to the length of your finger and heat them gently in the fire; and insert one into the patient's ear, and let him blow on it from his other ear, and press another stone upon the stone which is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the pain goes out, and thus will it all come out; and if you see that, take a straw and put one end into the ear, and heat the other end in the fire until the most painful straw is burned; then do the same again with other straws until all the pain goes out, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an object from the ear, if it is a small object such as a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the previous chapter. But if the object is large enough to be felt, administer extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest method to remove something from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms from the ears, if you treat them as we have said in the section on distillations and the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in the sun. If any worms appear, then catch them with fine tweezers; if they do not appear, then take the skin of a chicken where the comb is,
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the smallest end of the cautery into the ear according to the amount of pain from the ailment, then suck firmly on the tube; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then stop up the cotton tube as I said for the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven for worm treatment, and you will find them in the section on distillation; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, so that their shape is as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of silver or bronze with small holes beneath and open above for distillation; and to press the distillation into this instrument use a well-made bronze tool, and if you wish take a razor and wrap cotton around its tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you desire, into the chicken skin, and let the skin be in the ear; then put the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled into the ear; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be slightly warm as it is poured into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not work as well.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	on the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an opening in their ears; and the same thing happens to men due to the clogging of a wound, or due to pus forming inside the ear, and sometimes this clogging extends deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is only a slight blockage, which can be seen easily.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	When it occurs deeply and cannot be seen, it is a matter of great concern in various situations, and in such a case, one should hold the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane becoming apparent, then treat it according to its appearance.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and pointed in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the membrane is due to pus or some other substance inside the ear, then grasp it with a pair of fine forceps and squeeze gently until all the substance is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the growths are deep in the ear, then take a thin and subtle razor and heat it slightly in the fire, and then insert it into the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the itching that the patient feels deeply in his ear, pierce it slightly, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then insert a plug into the ear according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this each day until the wound is healed, or take a piece of cloth and moisten it in rose water, and powder with vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then you should remove the cloth and replace it with another moistened in cerotum made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then heal the wound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is bleeding, plunge a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the bleeding that are used for treating distilleries.
de la char des papieres	of the pulp of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul comes from papers when they are wet and dry, you should extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the tip of a spatulum from its roots; then put powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without skin, then cauterize with a subtle lens-shaped cautery, and the cautery after the incision is valuable; and many times they return, as long as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hailstones
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times they come out of the ears, things that look like hail in its form and hardness, and because of this, this disease is called "hail", and it is a collection of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the treatment is such: if the hail mutaes from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know, they then open it wide, then lightly peel each part, then pick it up with tweezers and cut it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, do not harm the patient; and if the slit is large, assemble it with a stitch, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not force it, for ointments will restore it at once.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hailstone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then reverse the paper, and the hailstones are held with tweezers, and covered and pressed from one side to another; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does no harm; and when the hailstone is covered, wipe away the pus with a clean cloth, and cure the area where the wound is until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is woven into the fabrics of papers, and this happens more to children than to anyone else, and it is very serious for them. They get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot bear to look at the light of the sun because their tears run down their faces; and because of this, they lie on their backs and sleep, and their papers are underneath their eyelids, which are moistened by the discharge and covered by the exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the eye with your fingers and feel the exinach coming out.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way to do it is that the sick person puts his head on top of the healthy one; and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, and then put it over him; and press with your fingers on both sides so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moist skin with a sharp spatulum, and do not make it larger than the wound made for the vein opening; and in various dispositions, exinach comes out of the slit according to the shape of a piece of white grease.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take out the entire piece of cloth with your fingers between your thumb and forefinger, and turn your hand to the right and left so that it is spread out; and be careful not to put anything in the slit, so that you do not come to the spatula all the way to the eye, so that you do not hurt it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound does not open at the beginning of the slit, then widen the slit slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten cloth in vinegar and water, and apply to the area, and extract with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind it down and put something on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cleanse the eye until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is a hot abscess in the eye, treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs of a different nature than usual, and they are enveillit, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases, such as tears, and softening of the paper and albugine, all of which lead to the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to treat them: by cauterization with fire, or by medicine applied to the eye, or by incision and stitching, or by caustic substances, depending on what is described in this chapter on cauterization.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary for you to place the head of the patient in your lap, then turn the paper on his eye to your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; but if not, then put an needle with thread through it from above; and have this close to the margin of the paper where the hairs are growing next to these hairs, and draw the thread across the paper to the top, and turn it over to the razor; then, on the part under the paper, under the hairs, all around, as much as the spatulum covers, from the large eyebrow up to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a little tent of cotton and linen underneath the paper, and sign a figure of an inch, like the shape of a myrtle twig, and still it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see rising above the paper which is split in two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if he has to cut, then one cuts a great quantity of the paper according to how soft the paper is; then they mark on all the spatumile along the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large nostril up to the small one; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs at the thickness of a root, then stuff the eye with one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape it all off; then sew together the two lips with a needle and fine thread of wool, and draw out the blood, and dry up any excess of the threads over the two nostrils with anything sticky, if you see fit to do so; if not, then don't worry about it, then leave the sutures and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without sutures using dry and constrictive things, because the paper lifts up at the wound's soudure and its joining together, but the sutures are painful (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: one marks the paper with a shape that is like the leaf of a myrtle, as we have described, with three curved notches according to the form given.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut away what is on top of the smaller forces evenly according to the form which is here:

de la porriture de l’oil	of the puffiness of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "alacrity" or warts comes in the eye, there are two ways of getting it: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or cutting or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to treat it is to split that sore, and loosen the edges of it, and put in tents made of linen, and keep it open until it is healed; and you must not use in its treatment anything which would dry it up and constrict it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but treat it with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or altée and flaxseed cooked in water, and ointments of diluted alkanet, and wrap a tent around it, and cure it thus.Et qu’il soit sanee, si est bon qu’on le cure de oignemens de la teneur d’alcanet, ou de saindore et de l’huile d’amandes dolces, ou d’autres oignemens amollissans.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the essence of your treatment is that you take care that it does not swell again according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is beneath, which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; the way to treat them is to take a needle with double thread, pierce it into the flesh, and then bring out the thread through both ears so that the thread comes out in two places on the skin. Then the skin will be pulled taut above the needle, and the cut will be held wide open by the thread.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez. Then remove the skin, according to the quantity that its edges are cut beneath it, from what follows the skin; then join the two separated parts and sew them up with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said with softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye

de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula

de l’issue de l’oil	from the output of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are completely open and there is no disturbance to the nose or diminution, you should ligature the patient; then bleed him, then apply cupping glasses or leeches without piercing, to suck out, then place over the eye a poultice made of acacia gum, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then compress the eye with bandages and drapes; the manner of the drapes is that you take quite soft drapes, and double each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye requires; then compress from above with a firm bandage, and repeat the cupping without piercing; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the ligature softens, you should compress it strongly; then remove the poultice after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, repeat the poultice, and the drapes, and the poultice, and the cupping until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the ruptura of a woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the woven cloth, then it opens up and appears like a grain of resin, and is frightening to look at; therefore, if you see it covering, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part underneath up to the part above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the part of the eyelid; and pierce the latter, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the area of the double thread and tie one part of the cloth around it, and compress it well; then remove the needle and place raw linen soaked in egg white over the eye; and leave it until the threads tear with the cloth, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is constrained by the cloth on each side in a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the eyes appear swollen, pierce them with a sharp needle that penetrates through the white of the eye, and draw out the fluid, then push the eyes back in and they will heal.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye socket
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not dangerous except for the lump which gathers in the eye, resembling water but is not; and the way to treat it is to make the patient sit upright on a chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides and move it until you see the lump come up towards your eyes; then let it be, and darken the light, and have the patient look at things as he used to; if the lump does not go down below, know that it is water, and if the lump is not apparent as we have said, take a needle from a thread.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatulum and press it against the conjunctive membrane where it meets the cornea and the corona, until the eye pops out; and when it is popped out, instil into the eye warm water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek and honey have been boiled, then treat it further with other remedies until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already spoken of the appearances of diseases in this division, and what should be done to pierce them; now act according to the state of health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your hands, turned away from the light of the sun, and hold the healthy eye closed and firmly pressed; then take in your left hand, if the eye is on the left, a piece of paper which has been soaked in warm water with honey or fenugreek, and in your right hand, if the eye is on the right, the instrument called «almagda»; then insert the tip of «almagda» into the white of the eye at the height of a hair from the edge of the pupil, towards the part where the tear duct drains; you will see the bone through the clear conjunctive membrane; then push the instrument to the depth of a hair from the edge of the black pupil, and express «almagda» firmly and repeatedly.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if water now runs down, the patient sees himself and the instrument before him.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a short rest, and if the water flows back up the second path, push it out with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not flow, gently twist your hand a little; then put some powdered gem in the eye again and remove the instrument.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then push into the eye cotton wool or lamb's wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white, and bind it with a clean cloth.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on powdered cumin mixed with plenty of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you must use the instrument called 'alberit', which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so you pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make the cut shallow, then put in the alum, as we have said; and when the work is finished, prepare for the patient the appropriate dark room, so that he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and he should avoid all movements, and eat light food, and not move his head or to the right or left, and he should be bound according to his condition for three days; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the bandage back on for seven days; and you should not do this during the hour of the incision or afterwards now, but you must wait until the water flows rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	if such an abscess comes, that you loosen the eye before the seventh day, and the address of he who soothes abscesses; and when it is appeased, then loosen the eye and put on its face a piece of gold to cover some wound, and let it remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and return to his own case; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Spain, who told us that in his country they used alum pierced, with which one sucked out the water, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the likenesses of the forms of almagest, because those who do not know them can see them; and they are properly made of brass:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the heads of these be of the same subtlety, and the points in four angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart upon the veins
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes they are born with various deformed limbs, from which there are some that look like scorpions at the end of the feet; and there are some with a limp with a dark-colored foot, and a clubfoot with a fair-colored one.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	With such a clubfoot, therefore, you should make the patient sit in your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils, and put the needle into those limbs, drawing them out; then touch that which you can withstand with a very fine needle at one end, until you know that the limb is entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains that cannot be covered, then open it with one of the subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without you are overwhelmed, or an abscess forms, then lances it as it should be; and if it is a malignant abscess, then hasten to cauterize it until the pus is drained and all the pus is removed, then pour in wine or water.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it works and moisture reaches the palate, you will know that he is healthy; and if moisture does not pass through as it should, you will know that there is bad blood in the bone above, for which instruments cannot reach to cut: therefore, you must take a fairly thick piece of linen thread and tie it with your fingers, leaving a gap of one or two fingers between each knot; then put the patient's nose on the thread at their own pace, and draw it through the nose into the mouth with scent until it reaches the palate; children often do this in school, and it is easy for anyone who wants to do it. Then hold the end that comes out of the nose in one hand, and the end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, pulling them gently so that they are even with each other.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the nails have corrupted the flesh, then draw out the nail, wipe away the blood, and moisten the nail in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the flesh; and then put a plug of linen in the nose for some days until it heals, and if there is need of dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, with which one distils oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it can be made of silver or brass, similar to an open lamp, with a handle, and it should also have a lid; and if you want, make a closed cane, and let the instrument be hollow for cleansing the ears; and it should have a handle at the end for holding it when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart upon the veins
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "tuberculosis" arises in the head of the veins, and it grows and becomes large, so that it is visible to look at; and therefore you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then place the hot cautery or medicine upon it; and if one delays cutting it until it has become large, then be wary if it is hard, discolored, and lacking in sensation: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess, because when one cuts it at any time, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due only to pressure, not discoloration, and you see that one can cut it all away, then evacuate the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the area of dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the vein is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in any of these cartilage wounds, it benefits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when it happens to someone, consider whether the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then stitch together the two lips at a seam, then heal it until it is healed; and if the lips are torn on both sides, you should scrape away all the parts of their skin until they heal, then sew together the two lips at a seam, and tighten them, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and burned incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of strong plaster or other binding plaster, and let it close up by itself, then heal it with ointment.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you use thread: either with needles as we said for sewing the belly, or with thread as I have already told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At times there are hard abscesses inside the lips, resembling grains of peas, both smaller and larger; therefore, you should open the lips, and cut on each nodule, and pinch it with tweezers, and scrape away any dry matter until the wound is cleaned out; then apply vitriol powder to the incision, and then use an astringent, and treat the area with poultices until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of gum disease
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call 'albulus'; you should hold it with tweezers, cut at its root, and let the blood or pus flow; then place powdered vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders, on the site; if the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, and this is the form for treating abscesses.
des sordens	Here is a translation of the provided text:
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Here is a translation of the provided text:
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating a toothache that you delay as little as possible in pulling the tooth, for there should be no excuse not to do so; for it is a very serious matter to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is compelled to pull, you must be certain of the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient and believes it is in the good tooth, and makes them pull out the healthy tooth; and even so, the pain does not leave because of this, as long as the evil tooth remains, for we have already seen this happen with these patients. And when you are certain that it is a toothache, then you should scrape around the tooth all around, opening the gum widely; then move it with your fingers or with thin tweezers little by little, until it is well loosened, then grip the tweezers tightly; and let the patient's head be between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Afterwards, pull out the tooth firmly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and rotten, you should fill the hole with a piece of cloth, and then gently pull it with tweezers so that it does not break when pulling; and one must work bleeding around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and leave a part of it behind, which will cause greater pain from the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of doing as ignorant surgeons do, who often break the tooth in their haste and audacity, and do not follow our advice; but sometimes they bring on great illness through infection from the roots that remain, or by breaking the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the socket with wine or garlic and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the socket; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of forceps, with which one pulls out teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick metal so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be well-made iron, and serrated to hold the gums.
de la racine des dens	from the root of teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in place, you should apply wet cotton soaked in butter for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then apply the tongs called "algefri", which make the shoulder look like a sick bird's beak; they should be made inside just like a file, and that is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tweezers, you must uncover the skin all around the root, and insert the instrument called "althali", that is, a splint, which has this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, that is good; if not, then you must use all the instruments, of which the forms come later:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should also use this instrument which has .ij. prongs, of which the shape is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front of teeth, and this instrument which looks like a large pair of tweezers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And have this instrument outside so that it cannot be broken, and know that many instruments for teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise subtle master finds by himself his instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, because there are many diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity. And if it doesn't break the cart or other bones, or it protrudes, then he searches for the instruments he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone so that it doesn't slip, but he can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with appropriate medicine. And if there is protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then use this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or ground down. So pull it out; and if there is abscess with the tooth, take this instrument of which the form is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron with a sharp point at its end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And push it in and out little by little due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent, and can be filed down, then file it with a special file as shown in the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file with which we make needles; and in filing, press gently, day after day, little by little, until it does not move, and then smooth it at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, one should file down the sharpness until it is even so that it doesn't cut the tongue or distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are crooked
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loose, either from blows or falling, and the patient cannot chew without pain, and you have treated them with constricting medicines which do not work, then they must be restrained by a gold wire; silver wire turns green and rusts, but gold never does. The wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, depending on the amount of space between the teeth. If you see the teeth moving, take the wire and wrap it double between two healthy teeth, then place the shoulder between the teeth that are loose, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then start the treatment again from the beginning, and gently tighten your hand until it does not move. The ligature should be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the teeth with tweezers, bring them together and place them between the healthy teeth so that they do not pierce the tongue; then leave them thus clenched as tightly as possible, and if they come apart, either the threads will break or he will tighten them with another thread; let him stay like this and function all his life, and this is how the teeth are formed and arranged in the healthy jaw, both the top and bottom sets, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth is missing, we replace it with a new one, as we have said; but only a wise and experienced person should do this, and sometimes we make a tooth out of cow bone and put it in the place of the defect, restraining it as we have described, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament, which comes under the tongue by nature, is born like that; sometimes it happens due to a wound, and the operation is such that you open the mouth of the patient, place his head on your healthy jaw, and pull out his tongue; then grasp the nerve of the broad ligament so that the tongue is dislodged from its socket, and if there is hardening or a nodule, it is due to an abscess, so you cut it with a sharp instrument and grasp the ligament; be careful not to pierce too deeply, lest you hit the artery underneath. When you are done, raise the vein with rose water and garlic, or cold water, then place a tent of linen under the tongue; and every night, paint the wound with a mixture of lead and vinegar so that the edges do not adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, then apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if the blood stops flowing, then cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this. Then treat the wound further until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel any pain, do not touch it, as it is a sore; and if it is inclined to blanching and there is moisture, pierce it with a needle, and drain it from both sides; and if bleeding occurs due to your treatment, apply powdered vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until you have removed everything. Then raise the area with garlic and salt, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses in the throat:
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there appear in the throat what are called "godath", which are properly called "almonds", and when you treat them as described above and they do not heal, then take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and a light color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it with iron, also because of the flow of blood; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will separate it, or it will burst on its own; and if it is of a white color and the root is thin, then have ready the instrument for covering, but first look to see if the abscess has settled and is pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit facing the sun, and have his head in your lap, and open his mouth and press the tongue down with your fingers, and hold the instrument between your hands, and shape it according to its form; it should be made of silver or thin brass like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Then you press the tongue against all this instrument, and you will see the abscess; take a needle and insert it into the almond, and draw it out above as much as you can; then draw some threads from the cloth with it, then cover the instrument with which this shape is made, so that it looks like a hook; and even though the heads are curved, and one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then cover it with tongs, of which this is the shape:
