Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be cut in one part and left uncut in the other; and when you have lanced one of the tonsils, lance the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, gargle with water, or scalded pomegranate peels, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses develop in the throat besides the two tonsils, so lance them in the same way as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had almost all her throat closed up, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway which was blocked, and she could not eat or drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had forced out two holes through the nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened therefore at once, and inserted a hook into one of the holes, then drew it out, and removed a great deal of pus; then I pierced another hole in the other nostril, and cleared her throat and pressed her tongue down; afterward, I inserted the hook into the abscess, and removed some of it, and only a little blood came out; thus was the passageway of the woman's throat opened up, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting into the abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, filling up the space which I had emptied, so that it became very large; therefore I lanced it and cauterized it within the throat; thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and she was in God's hands after me.
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the iris descends to the eyeball, and it is swollen and it is long, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is thick and round below, then it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the eye's abscess is pacified, and it is thin, then you should cut it; and that which is round and not long, and is blood-red or flesh-colored or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in it for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner which I have described, of its whiteness and length, you should make the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it underneath, and cut at the end of the two instruments that I described for cutting into the two almonds.Et la cope a li II estrumens qui sont de l’auter costé, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument susdit, et si le laisse un peu de temps ains qu’il se remuë.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover anything more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; because if you cover more, it weighs down the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two testicles, and heal it until it is cured.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use the cauterization of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The nature of the cautery is as follows: take hot iron and apply it to the part that needs cauterization.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your lap, and then presses his tongue to the instrument that we described in the chapter on cauterization, and mixes it with quicklime, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the application of this instrument, from which comes its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle at its head where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and the instrument is applied to the whole medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine flow out of his mouth and do not descend into his throat and windpipe. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, until you see it swell and the burning of the medicine is soothed; then take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the cotton around the eye, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; do this often until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry for four or five days. If you need to renew the cautery with medicine, do so, and after the cautery, wash the area around the eye with cold water, and treat it with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is healed by fumigation in this manner, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. The pot should be well glazed with strong clay, and the handle of the instrument should be bent according to this shape:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	Whether it is made of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes is pushed into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is deadened; then repeat often until the eye dries out, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not do this except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put a chicken egg inside the end, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; because the chicken egg does not allow the vapor to burden the mouth, and it is a salutary remedy together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; so you should treat what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all your instruments, so that you move the object; and if it does not become apparent to you and is lodged in the throat, then you must make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a morsel of dry bread; and attach a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the spot, it will get stuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take an instrument of soft lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be bent at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have its tip lifted up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, or he will vomit everything, nor push the bone inside; and move so that the patient swallows the instrument, so that he can move where the object is stuck; then he swallows it down, or pulls it out with all his strength, equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the bloodletting is the medicine, as I said in the division, through the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the patient's throat in the sunlight, then press their tongue with the instrument I told you about.And if you see that the throat is very red, it is a good sign; but if you see that it is pale, it is a bad sign; then press harder until you feel resistance, and do not let go until you feel the pulse in the instrument.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see a vein, draw it gently with a small hook, or with subtle tweezers that are fit for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not effective, take a piece of horsehair and insert it into the throat of the patient, then heat the end of the hair with hot iron, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the illness is due to water, all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with his hand frequently; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will subside.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not subside as we have said, smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument I described for smoking the throat; do this many times, for it will subside without bleeding.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fume is that you put charcoal in a pot with a lid pierced in the middle, and the instrument's head in the hole, then blow your smoke, and the patient puts his mouth on the pipe, closes his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but goes to the blood; and the blood will fall soon, and if it does not, then restart the smoke many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salted things, and drink nothing; and then he will need to urinate through this regime.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And if he does not urinate, then strengthen the body with hot baths and by anointing the body; it is good for him to stay in the sun and eat things that are warm. And if his body is very cold, then bathe his head first so that he does not move, then bathe his limbs; and if he still does not urinate, then bathe him all over, and let him eat and drink warm things. And if it goes as we have said, know that the blood has withdrawn.
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what the memories come here after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways, one is in its own appearance, and of what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for warts on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses on the head are different from those in the buttocks, and the abscesses of the fleshy parts are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own method of treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if one should not pierce an abscess until the pus is mature according to its course; and some must be pierced when they are crusty and do not die according to their course, such as those that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess comes near a joint, and one lets it be until it is completely pus-filled around the joint, often the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.Et si li apostemes sont creuz et la carne demure entor, tant qu’il n’est pas creuz jusques a la chair morte, tant il ne se guarit mie; et quant il sont creuz jusques a la carne morte, alors si se guarit.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where the abscess is near the principal member, if you delay piercing it until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; and if it is near the fundament, one should pierce it so that it may ripen; but one must not pierce an abscess without digestion being completed, except for one that is near the fundament, lest it burst inside and become elongated, and a fistula results, taking a long time to heal.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time for piercing an abscess that is ripe according to its nature, and this occurs when the pain subsides, and the fever lessens, and the swelling and redness decrease, and there is less discharge and pressure from the head of the abscess, along with other signs. One should pierce where the abscess is largest and where there is the most discharge; and the piercing should be done in a vertical direction from the body, especially if the abscess is on the arms or legs, or near joints, affecting nerves and arteries, and in all similar cases where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	For those who bend, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to leave the piercing until it is consolidated with digestion completed, as we have said.Si tu veilles apercer le charnut, si doit tu faire si qu’il ne vienne fistule; car li charnus sont de nature froude et fraiz, et li muesciles se desfaissent promptement et la chair reste fraide.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it earlier, the body's venom will flow out and fill with foul matter, and the lips and depths may harden.Et se il est delez la plote, si doit tu le percer ainsois qu’il soit meurs et non pas avant ceu; car si tu le perces ant ceu qu’il soit meurs, li venim qui sort de lui, si est froude, et ne peut se confermer en grant termine, et est longes et durs.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if an abscess is opened according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses with large incisions, and many slits according to the appearance of their size; and if in such abscesses one should cut out the core and cover it over when it has become like a drum skin and died down, then one should do as is done with blisters: and if there are some that are split into three angles, and others that are covered like the leaf of a myrtle, as are abscesses of the bowels; and if there are some in which one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those that have no head, as with a superficial abscess, one should pierce it directly; and when the abscess is large and has formed a great boil, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but some of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this repeatedly, little by little, until all the pus comes out; likewise if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying child, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced sometimes jump out of the belly with the exit of the bowels, which inadvertently kills the patient, and you do not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, wash the wound, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a flat ulcer, apply tents made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many openings, you should put a tent in each one so that they press against each other; and if you have cut into the skin around the abscess and covered it all around, you should fill it with dry cotton or rags of linen free of moisture, and bind it for up to three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bloodletting occurs in your work, bring cold water and a wet cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, bring relief and treatment, and the powders I have mentioned earlier in this book; and if it is in the winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should place wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil over it; and if it is in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for a third of a day, as we have said; then loosen the abscess, wash and treat it, as appropriate, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now you must know generally about the treatment of abscesses; I have already told you how one should go about treating abscesses, and now see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the neck come small abscesses, and they are caused by insects that live in our clothing, just like the lice on a goose, and there are many variations of them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and smooth where there is moisture as well as pulsation; and there are some that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contraction.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you must first test all instruments called "syringes", from which the forms come later, whatever they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it will flow out from above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is expelled, it scabs without leaving anything behind from the skin that contains the moisture, for it returns again if nothing is left there; then plunge cotton into Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply this to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who stay through the night will heal.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin again with the cotton, as before, on the second and third day, until you know well that it does not remain at night; then heal the wound with ointment that is suitable, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, cut it according to this form, from the center; and pour out your fingers, and scrape off all around, and put all your treatment in pulling out the cotton where he lies; and if the artery makes a contrary sound, do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure as I have told you.Car la piere se tuit apesentement ne fuist traie hors du corps, ains doit demourer lor, et n’est pas grant disconfort a li membraire; car de l’un est le piere, et de l’auter est li sang; et s’il ne fuist pierous, si doit estre curé com je t’ai dit.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on a painful, moist abscess is lighter, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses have no moisture in their heads, and I copied an abscess from the head of an old woman; and found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and if one had cut into it, they would have made a wound just like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, those that come from the heads of children and from the roots of the ears, the opening should be made in the most dependent location so that the pus can flow out; and they should be treated as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses come on the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and they are large, and they are intertwined with each other.Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And every scrofula is properly within its coat, as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the similitudes of these scrofulae are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and will not obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	So with the one that you see has a good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and is even on all sides and is not sunken into the vessels of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not deep; so you must cover it from above, and scrape away at every part, and make the two lips of the wound even, as needed, as we have said regarding abscesses of the head; and draw it a little bit at a time, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatula or forceps so that the hand slips, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you pack the vein or artery and it will not allow you to work, then put in the wound vitriol ground, or any powder that stops bleeding, and compress the wound; and let it be until the abscess is pacified, and the wound softens, and begins to discharge pus.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you finish it; then examine with your finger if any small scrofulous tumors remain, and scrape them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, you must not pack that scrofula at its root, but ligature it with a strong double thread, and let it drop without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut away the entire scrofula, then you should bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no longer any surplus due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should proceed to cut away at the root of it, pull it outward, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula that hold surplus, pierce where it appears to be dying; and pierce it thus as that one before was said, depending on it, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what is left of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then cure it with ointment soaking up pus, until it is healed.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient wrote and spoke of the incision of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squint, the flap of the throat called the 'epiglottis' should be cut; and this is done by those who have hot abscesses in their mouths, throats, or both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it below three circles or four a little slit crosswise between the two circles, or according to the amount of the slit in the hyoid bone; and those places are suitable for the splitting of the epiglottis that there is no pus, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should then split the skin of the throat to the base of the tongue, and cut through the cartilage until he reaches the jawbone; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then stitch up the wound as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the artery of the jaw which jumps out through the broken place, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which you doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the heart, and sew it up entirely without the cartilage; then administer remedies that promote scabs, until they are healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says to do this only as long as the throat is completely choked, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath continues.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then stitch up the epiglottis so that the patient can breathe through the wound and thus be guarded from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the violence of the disease had passed, which passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, once it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young maiden take a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the tendons in her neck; and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it had not oozed or flowed further than the throat, and the vein had stopped bleeding.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was cured; and the maiden had no more pain in her throat, and returned to her normal state; therefore, I say that one should not fear cutting into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This type of abscess is called "gorge hernia", and it is a large abscess the color of a purple-red, and it occurs mostly in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; the natural kind has no pus.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental type comes in two forms: one is similar to a cyst, and the other is like an abscess that arises from an artery; there is fear involved, and one should not attempt to force it with anything except on a small one, and test and probe throughout the entire opening: if you find it to be just like a cyst, and it cannot be drained in any way, then cut into it as one cuts into a cyst, and treat it all the way to its core, if there is nothing else; and probe thoroughly, and heal it as it should be healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe to you. Now I must explain the difference between a dislocation and a fracture.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is continued fever, as long as the ebullition has not passed and the porridge is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a fracture, there is no fever, pain, or swelling; it is a discolouration of the skin which is specific to the affected area and starts as a bruise that becomes larger. There are two types: one dry, one moist, and their colours vary as I have described in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the nose, that you test and inquire first with all the instruments which are called "forceps", according to what its shape will come to in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	To probe an abscess, press on the softest spot you find and slowly push your finger in until you feel resistance from the pus, then remove your finger and look for pus to emerge. Continue this process according to the size of the abscess; then extract the pus with a instrument, taking care not to burst it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If yellow pus emerges, treat it as described for other abscesses. If no pus comes out after probing, know that it is a solid mass; make an incision in the shape of a cross and grab it with tweezers, then lightly scrape away the surrounding skin and pull out the mass. If you cannot remove it all at once, cut it out piece by piece so that nothing remains inside.Et li nout de la cotte est selonc la color dou cors; si le corps est moiste, il est gras et blanc ou jaune ou noir; si le corps est sec, il est dur, sec, brun ou noir.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it remains unchanged, then the nose returns many times; and if a little of it remains, and the wound troubles you not, then employ some corrosive powders on the wound, and constrain the wound, and place upon it things that soothe an abscess hotly, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the nose is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and cure it with that which causes flesh to grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beats against you or another, quickly apply ground vitriol and leave it for two or three days until the wound suppurates and the bleeding stops; then return to the cupping as before.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of cutting instruments for fistulas, and they come in three varieties: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of these, called 'albaret', one called 'breb', and there are also three types: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of warts are very varied, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and some warts have two curves in three ways; and some have three curves and are also in three ways; and some have two curves, and warts with only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these tools are sharp, and some only cut from one side, so that the vein or nerve is not cut; and these intruded tools are placed in many places, so that the patient does not perish when opening abscesses; and there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are not used except in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and in similar places; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling a slice of a fig, according to this form, with which blood is stopped.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and they put it sometimes in the place that heals by cutting the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes they mend according to this large form;
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	At times the breasts of some men swell when they begin to become rotten, and appear like women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen. And if one wishes to cure them, then it is fitting that he should proceed according to this form from b to g .
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape off the fat and employ medicine on the wound in layers, then sew up the two lips of the wound, and treat it until it is healed. And if the breast sags down and becomes soft due to its size as happens with women, then split it into two at the top along two similar incisions; have one lip of one incision attached to the other at the end of both incisions so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from b to g. Then scrape off the skin between the two lips and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment until it is healed; but if it is not healed or the incision is not fully made due to the patient's discomfort or blood flow, then you must fill the wound with wet cotton saturated in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remnant and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus inside the abscess is drained, plug the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day. Then remove all the cotton and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are like scrofula, then treat them as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is closed, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is open and the skin above it, there often arise abscesses, and likewise in the vein is swollen and abscessed; and so one knows it when it is from the artery, for the abscesses are long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel tugging; and when it is from the vein, there is a loss of feeling and swelling appears; and it is folly to cover this abscess, especially when it is beneath the armpits and on the arms and neck and in many other places, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one must avoid the cautery of iron and that which is on top must also be avoided, and in that which is swollen from an artery, cut through the skin where the long vein is; then cut the artery away from the bones, and separate it from the veins, so that it is uncovered; then insert a needle underneath, and have it pierce all the way to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then tie off the place between the two threads with an introducer so that the blood within flows out and the abscess is relieved; then apply the cautery as if it were a bow, until the ligature slips; then cure this with ointment, and when it has healed, cure it again with tenting and ointments. And if the abscess is from the vein, you must dye your hand with what comes from the abscess to all of the skin, then insert another needle underneath where you are holding your hand, and have it pierce through, and tie a double thread to it, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie off the abscess, as I told you, at one of the two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will slip out, insert another needle underneath all of the abscess, at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in three places; then cover the abscess so that the excess flows out, then cover the excess from the skin and leave what is tied; then place a moistened cloth in wine and oil, and administer tenting and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also, as abscesses come in the artery and vein, they also come to the nerves when they are hurt, or through excessive exertion, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and all over where there are joints, and it is a deep abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain; and when one presses on it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not throughout the body but under the skin; and it is mute in all parts, and does not move forward or backward, or down or up, and that which is in joints should not be covered with iron: by chance there might be a contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, treat with a poultice.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, grasp it with tweezers and cut off its root; and if it is large, pierce it with a needle, and scrape it out, then cut away the flesh and sew up the wound, and let it heal.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At times it occurs in bellies and nowhere else; it is a disease called 'mushroom' because of its resemblance to mushrooms: the roots are thin while the excreta are thick. There are small ones and very large ones. I saw a man who had two on his belly that looked more like mushrooms than anything else, with no difference between them; they were white and had thin roots, and were slightly split, and moisture ran from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces; the treatment for the incision is that you examine whether the disease is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with thin roots; then cup with a wide spatulum, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For often there are excessive bloodlettings when cutting, and if the bleeding stops, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient is frightened and fearful of the incision with the iron, then take a well-prepared thread and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then restrain it, and do not stop tightening the thread until he cuts the joint, and it comes away without effort; and if the roots are thick, then be careful when cutting for the belly, but you can certainly cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and beware of cutting the scrotum which is of a foul color and poor sensation and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the cure for cancers below.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil has burst
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or ulcer, and is on the abdomen and in some of the bowels, as it happens in other routs, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or from wind; and if it is from the rout of the ulcer and from the discharge of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and it discharges in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestines, then it will be very diverse; and when pressed with the fingers, it retracts, and then returns, and sometimes it is constricted, and it increases in size at the entrance to the bath due to intense exertion.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a slight thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, nor does it constrain at all; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and they are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, there is a sound when touched, and the actions indicate that you should look to see whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you need to let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Because there is doubt and fear as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is in the intestine or bowels, then instruct the patient to tighten his belt and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the bump; then instruct him to lie still between your hands, then go around the area that you have marked all around the spasticity, then press down on half of the abscess above the large nail; then tie it tightly with a strong thread or strong silk rope, and let the patient's hand hang free; then open half of the abscess over the string, and insert your finger, and squeeze the intestine; if you find it caught in the string, release it, and squeeze the intestine out of the abdomen; and if you find the bowels, grab them at the nail and cut off the excess; and if the artery acts contrary, or the vein, then go around well, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads through them, and pierce what you have made in a cross so that you make a perforation; then squeeze the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see any, remove the needles, and leave the wound as it is until it drains, and cut away the dead flesh by itself; or scrape it when it becomes thin and drainable, then treat the wound as needed, and cauterize the wound.
dou chancre	from which ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have described in the division of similarities of ulceration, and how one should work with medicines, and how one should avoid the cure of iron; and we speak of ulcer in the genitals, and great caution is required in its cure, and the ancients said that when ulcers are in places where they can be cut, such as ulcers in breasts, and in similar places, then all of it must be removed when it is in the beginning. And when it is large and old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never been able to heal any of them, nor has anyone ever healed them before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile sometimes; then make him bleed if he has manifest fullness; then open the wound .i. good place to do the work; then cut your oncines or cancer, and the head from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow out completely, and squeeze well the place with your hand or something, and if the bleeding makes you opposite to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood vessels are burned; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the appearance of dropsy, and how the gathering of fluid occurs, as well as the signs of each appearance, and the treatment using medication, and that which is treated with iron. Only two types, tympany and hydrops, should be treated with iron; it is a dangerous procedure. Therefore, when treating this type of dropsy called "tympany" with medications, if the patient is weak or has other illnesses besides dropsy, such as constipation and similar conditions, do not use iron, as there is a risk involved. However, if the patient is strong and only suffering from dropsy, and is neither too young nor too old, proceed as follows: lift the patient upright, and press on the abdomen to force the fluid down towards the feet. Then, use the spathula with thorns according to this procedure:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be two parts to this.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be two parts. And let it not be so sharp that it pierces all the way to the intestine when inserted, nor can it cause bleeding; then examine whether the hydropsy is pressed against the intestines: if it is due to liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the armpit at a distance of three fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, then make the incision on the right side. And it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the excess fluids do not flow towards the weaker area; then pierce the skin with your instrument, and insert it, and leave your hand on the spatumile between the skin and the syphilis as you would when skinning, to a depth of one fingernail or more; then pierce the syphilis until the spatumile comes out at the desired location, which is where the water is located, then pull it out and insert this instrument from which the mold will emerge.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is similar to a silver needle, and is made of bronze or lightweight brass, and has a small hole in the lower part; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other, and one on each end; and the head is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes make when shaping a quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top is the alamenum, so that when the instrument comes to a boil, it descends immediately upon the instrument; empty it therefore half or a third full, for if you empty more than is appropriate at that hour, by chance the patient may die from the shock of the liquid, or he may faint, or he may approach death; but empty it according to the quantity of his strength, and according to what the dispositions of the strength of the sick person indicate, and his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and hold the liquid, which is now held by the membrane that blocks the hole in the syringe, about which I have spoken, so you pierce it according to this manner; then reintroduce the instrument the next day if you see he can bear it, and withdraw a little liquid; do this every day, but be careful not to overdo it while there remains even a little liquid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the illness, let him drink a lot of water, and then use the cure of burial or hot sand, and through much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if he becomes sick from drinking; and use medicines that dry up his body until he is healed, and cauterize his stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the foreskin of the penis:
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born without a foreskin, or with a small one that is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If necessary, pierce it immediately with a very thin and sharp instrument according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put a thin plug of lead into the opening and tie it there for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, remove the plug and let him urinate, then replace the plug; but sometimes this is not necessary, because the urine that comes out will open the foreskin.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	Those whose hole is small, if they are treated with the plaster of lead white, as we have said, it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hole in their place are bloated, because some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating before they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach the glans, and this is a serious illness.
