Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes the child comes out feet first, or through the chest or shoulder, or the arms, or through the belly or back; and it can also get stuck in the neck and be delivered in various other bad positions; therefore the midwife must be wise and cunning in such matters, and beware of mistakes and disappointments, and I will show you all the different positions and how to assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out head first in a natural way, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let her sit on a stool or be held by women; and let her drink the juice of roasted oil or fenugreek, and then let the midwife insert the little spatulum, of which I will now describe the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the naches, and press on its nail until the moisture that is inside flows out; and press the belly of the woman until the child comes down, and if it does not come down, then the woman must be enema with a mixture of fenugreek and oil of six mint; then make her press and sneeze with condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now let the child come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, then you must gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot go in, put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet up; then stand the chair on the ground, and hold one hand on the woman so that she does not shit while standing; and if the hands cannot go in, and the child is dead, then grip the hands with the knife which was mentioned before, and extract the child, and reset likewise.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child giving birth on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is born on its feet, it should be pushed up; and then it is turned little by little until it is straightened out; then grab it by the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to its hips, instruct it to be grabbed, and make it sneeze from the neck; if it jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't jump as we have said, then move it little by little until it returns to its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have described, take musk, rose oil, and gum dissolved, and grind everything in a mortar; then put this ointment on the mother's navel and let her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is soft down there, put the myrrh collar around her waist and leave it for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and squeeze her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for now the child will come out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's delivery upon his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, the midwife should gently place her hands on the child's back; then she should lie the child on its side, with its feet hanging down, and let it lie on its bed; and she should gently bend its hands, and then press its hands onto its belly, and lift up its bottom, so that it is facing downwards; and if the child does not cry out, she should take its feet and move them about, and then move its belly upwards, and push in with her hands; and she should rock the child gently; and she should tell the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the baby's birth, which comes out wide enough for one hand to pass through
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I will describe how to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then let her sit on the bed, and raise her legs straight up; then apply the medicine that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then let her sit on a chair, and then try to bring back the hand; and deliver the child in its natural position, and make her sneeze, and tell her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the emergence of the child above his neck, and has his hands spread out, and his face turned towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I want the patient to hold his hand still, then slowly turn it and move it slightly; and when it is even, he should apply a poultice of mustard and oil, as we have said, then instruct him to move it slowly; and when you have done this, have him sit on a chair, and instruct him to clap his hands; and make him sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all of the afterbirth
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way all over the body, then scoop up the afterbirth with your fingers until the fluids are expelled; and if the baby sticks to his mother's face and neck, scrape it off so that it is not retained and the baby dies; then put the baby back inside, making sure he is placed as he should be, and instruct the woman to clap her hands a few times: then gently pull on it.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the exit of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange creatures, and do not live if they are touched; I know that they multiply, and are separated by the wind which blows them, and are attached to the earth; and sometimes they issue forth as naturally as a tail, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge strongly, then the surgeon must act quickly and skillfully as we have said, and make the incisions subtly, and do whatever is necessary for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the sea as one, two, three, four, five, six, or seven, and sometimes more, up to fifteen, and they are all shaped like children according to the measurement of the glorious sage, and the surgeon must know this because a similar thing might happen to him; so he should act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child or a swollen belly, as I have said in the section on obstetrics, and there is no progress, and you must resort to manual extraction; then you should know if the woman is of sound health and does not have any fear of death; then you should make her lie on her back with her head tilted downward and her legs lifted up; and the surgeon should apply the ointment to two parts, or have her lie in bed so that she is not pulled down by the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils infused with myrrh, fenugreek, and flax seed, then anoint the surgeon's hands with these oils and unguents; then insert the fingers gently into the womb, and touch the places where the child is expected to emerge; if the child is positioned for a head delivery, insert the finger into the vagina or anus, or under the jaw, or along the sides of the throat, or under the beard, or in the armpit, or near the ribs, or the hip joints; and he should apply the ointment to his right hand and place the bandage between his fingers on his left hand, and insert his hand gently, and touch the places we have mentioned, until he reaches the empty space; and this is the shape of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then pierce into the other joint, or the third, if you need it, so that the extraction is even; and then they are even as they move from one side to another, for them to come out, and the joints bite to hold them in place, as is the form.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if some part remains, then anoint the joint with oil, and put it in that part, and pull out the other part; and if nothing remains, then put this joint or a higher one, and do this until everything comes out strong.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be pulled back because of the tightness, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it comes out; then put the hook in the joint of the wrist or the elbow, and so you should do to the other hand and to the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is constricted in the birth canal, or if there is a sharp pain gathered at the top, then you must use the spiny spatula between your fingers, and pierce the head and extract the fluid; or draw it out with the instrument called "almidach", from which the mold comes with the instruments in the chapter that follows this one; and likewise do if the child has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with tongs, and if the head pops out and is forced, it will split, so that the moisture that is in the birth canal comes out; and if it cannot come out, then pierce it in pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is above his feet, then the pull is light, and the direction to the mouth of the wound is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If it is constricted in the abdomen or foot, you should loosen it with the hand wrapped in a cloth; and open up the abdomen or foot so that the moisture inside can flow out; if other parts are stuck and the bowels remain, put his hand into the wound and pull it out to the mouth of the wound; then he inserts the thumb or two fingers and pulls outward; if the mouth of the wound is constricted by a hot abscess that has formed there, one should not work on it, but apply moist and greasy substances; one can also administer poultices, and use warm and soothing water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If the child is on its side and you can get it to lie down flat, then treat it as we said for a living child; if one cannot do this, pull it out in pieces, leaving nothing behind of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the patient is suffering from abscesses that occur in the bowels, and bleeding occurs, then it should be restrained with water, and other remedies administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then another was sewn onto her, and the other one died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she got an abscess in her armpit, which swelled so much that it opened, and began to discharge a lot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long and hard, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attractive plaster, and out came a bone, and after a few days some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very amazed, for I thought that bellies did not have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found bones inside, until the woman was in a better state; and she lived like this for a long time, and then she died of an illness from that place; and I only remembered this chapter because when a master encounters something strange, he should know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	how to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, to which one adds the books; and at .2. turns of .2. knees of .2. lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the constrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the tool should be two fingers wide, and its edges should be rounded, and one palm and a half long; and in both sides there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are fixed in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the wound to open it when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of tongs; and has two adjustments on each jaw, as you see, one palm-length long, and two digits wide; and when you see open the wound by all the instrument, then let the woman lie on her bed, with her feet hanging and her legs spread, then close the two adjustments together in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with tongs similarly, according to the amount that you see open the mouth of the wound, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated, and they have many similarities; and when the practitioner has prepared them, the action is more rapid and higher in status among people due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair over the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath and then sneeze forcefully, and squeeze your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she vomits through this action, that is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot and make an opening in the lid, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as comfrey, rue, anis, camomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked in water over fire; then put one end of a tube into the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and apply it so that the vapors enter the wound; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then remove the pus gently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she still has it after this treatment and it does not go away, instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand with oil of sesamum or with a poultice of alder, and then place it in its natural state, and seek out the secondine; and when she finds it, she should grasp and stretch it gently little by little, so that the wound does not hurt on extraction; but she must move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and be dislodged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the wound is narrow, we have spoken of the treatment of sneezing and of the fume of herbs; and if it is not from anything that we have said, be careful that you do not fool around with the enema; but it is appropriate that what is at the mouth of the wound, that you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with a four-drug ointment; then she will defecate and recover, and come out; but nonetheless, when she defecates, an evil odor comes to the stomach and head, and injures the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So you should use suitable fumigations: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The instrument used to fumigate the woman for retained afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like glass in appearance, and the thin end is placed in nature, and the wide ends are placed over the fire; and the fume is applied to the charcoal, and the wart until it is waste, and another begins.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foreskin pierced, but the penis is blocked by a thin membrane; so it is necessary that at the baptismal font, she pierces this membrane with her fingernail, and does not pierce it with a needle, and leave the bandage so that it does not touch it; then place it in milk moistened with wine and oil, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, insert a wooden peg into the hole and leave it for several days, then remove it when the child wants to move around.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stemming comes from a wound or abscess suddenly; so it must be stopped suddenly: then it should be treated as we have said with the wooden peg.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodules, and grow larger than those that come from within the anus, or in the space between the two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodule becomes old, it opens, and usually discharges a white or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are piercing; they are perceived by what comes out of them, either through defecation or flatulence, and sometimes a little jumps out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they can reach the joint of the thigh, and all the way to the scrotum.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows a piercing fistula in the anus, and not a non-piercing one; it is when you push your finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle made of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no bending.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has bending, insert a thin tent made of lead or horsehair into the fistula until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out through the opening, either defecation or flatulence, as we have said, then know that it does not pierce; so hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula penetrates up to the bladder or the urethra, urine leaks out and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced as far as the joint of the thigh, then the vein will flow as far as the spot; if there is a kink and the pain is felt around, then it will bend there, and ointments and remedies will not help; in these persisting fistulas, there is no cure but labor and the vanity of foolish remedies that are applied.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not persisting and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced; the patient lies on his back, and you lift his legs up to his thighs, and bend his thighs toward his belly; then pierce a vein with an iron rod, or with lead if there is a kink, until you know where the vein is.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it in the buttocks, then you must push your index finger in there, if without feeling that the vein has pierced through; and it should be exposed where you feel the swelling or the flesh, then you know it is persisting; one should not work on it unless they can heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can nonetheless heal some of them, although this rarely happens; and the aid one provides is to scorch the cautery sutilly according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and pour it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches the rectum; and do this two or three times, until you know that these falsified hairs have been burned, which look like a bird's feather; and then treat with tented moistened wool, until those hairs come out; then treat with ointment to join and seal.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent goes in and does not pierce all the way to the rectum, but there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of pus or of syphilitic material, and you see the fistula following under the covering towards the anus; then cut off at the beginning of the fistula, and pour in before the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be released, and fall out; then pluck out those falsified hairs that look like a bird's feather, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus flows out, and cuts between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two opposing things: namely, the burning of the joined flesh, and the stanching of blood and the drying of moisture; then the treatment of moist tents with butter or ground substance until the liquid flows out from under the burned flesh; then treat the wound with quick-setting ointments on hard charred flesh, and these are dry remedies.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to a point from the fundament, and is removed from the body, put your finger in it and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there is thread or char between them, or it is about to pierce through, then there is no hope but by one of three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut down to the bone, or if you can, insert tents and treat as before; and do not go too deep that you do not cut into the lining holding the foundation, and let the discharge come out through another opening; then treat as before; perhaps it will heal. Or remove that covering and cleanse after it has been cut away from the foundation, by tent or other pointed instrument; then scald the burned flesh in the wound, as much as you can; then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula open in the area away from the foundation: then it is a lighter burden on the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes they are fistulas like this: and it is when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation from which the skin is above, take a tent pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And thread a twisted thread through it, and put the tent all the way through the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is bleeding inside the margin of the foundation, then pull out the thread from that hole so that you put your finger in the foundation; and pull the end of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and strain one against the other, and leave it for a day or two; and sometimes restrain them, until the threads cut through the flesh that is between them, and separate; then cure the wound until it is healed and cleaned.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce through, then make it pierce in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to cover the wound with a bandage until it is completely healed, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spiny spatula used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, because one does not want to cut what one should not cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some discharge blood, and there may be one or more, and they are outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes there is a little green water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body; and the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to strain to go to the toilet until the anus opens and the threads appear; then be quick, and grasp it with tweezers or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if the nails cannot hold it due to moisture, they are grabbed with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and apply some hot powder that is in place of cautery; or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, then treat other hemorrhoids until it is healed; and if the anus cannot open, give the patient a strong and sharp enema to cleanse what is inside the anus so that it can open easily; when the patient strains and the threads come out of the anus, the treatment is easy; and you grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, cut them, then treat them as we have said until it is healed and fears incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	One must administer the stitch in the following manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle; then draw the thread through to the top and push the needle through from the other side; bring both ends of the thread under the needle, and keep it slack; then tighten the thread, tie a knot, remove the needle, and do the same for all the others; leave one to stem the flow of blood; then place a damp cloth moistened with rose oil or ceratum on the wound, apply pressure, and instruct the patient to rest; then let him stay like that until he passes gas, and when it has passed, treat the wound with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the bowels or anus
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is a drying up of fluids in the intestines, and due to a constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine avails not.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	One must cut away at the edge of a blister or hangnail with a spike, so that it does not become moist; then treat it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot dry, then restart the scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals well, and is scraped; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance formed under the body, and they go very deep; and sometimes the frost bites them, and one feels them as if dead from trembling, and they come throughout the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane of goose feather or a strong vulture feather and place this cane on the trembling so that the purple circle covers the trembling all around; then turn your hand over the whole cane so that you cup it all around the trembling, pushing it deep inside, and pull out the trembling by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit to make a cane of bronze or iron according to this form, and let it be slender underneath and drawn out on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, in order to hold it with the finger, and squeeze it. And if you see fit, cauterize the vein as it is before in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	on the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of molten bronze or steel; and sometimes one is made from these small and large instruments, according to the person to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are administered for the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, or the belly is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is an incision where the belly is bound, as you see, and the anus is inside pierced; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is made of a beast's bladder or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there is one inch of space, then insert into these holes a strong thread, twisting it in an X or spiral shape all around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then clysterize. And this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white or similar, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes his two hands together, so that they are both empty, then pull out the catheter, and let the patient lie on his side, and if the medicine wants to come out, then he should hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterwards, it is even more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cleanse him of stomach sickness, and the medicine rushes out, then cleanse him again until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or an abscess, then the catheter should be as fine as for a child; and it is the subtle type of catheter that is pressed against the skin.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will discuss the cures with the hands and with medicine, according to the situation.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are the striking of a stone, or cutting with a sword or knife, or piercing with a lance or pole or arrow, or similar objects; and they can occur anywhere on the body, like a wound on the neck, or head, or leg, or stomach, or liver, and similar organs. I will tell you how to cure each type of wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the head, because the memory will return in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, you should take care if it is from a blow from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you easily doubt a hot abscess: then make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and prevent the patient from drinking wine and eating heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine on the wound if a hot abscess comes, and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound if all its blood is out and it has not been moved by the air; and if the fire has moved it, then put some ointments on it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by sutures, then bring them together by stitches, as I will describe for wounds in the belly, at the ribcage.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be touched, and it holds only by a little bit, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as testes and cooked wheat, also as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pus in the skin, and it does not reach the bone, then cut away the pus all around, and let it drain out, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which does not clot, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: you must apply this powder that cauterizes so that the burn has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of making the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and make the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins to all its flesh; and then bind it well, and leave it without being loosened, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes cautery is done with chalk alone when incense and dragon's blood are not available, but the wound is cauterized nonetheless.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the burn has moved the wound, indeed in that case, do not apply any of this powder to it; but apply some digestive ointments, or a poultice made from barley flour and water and honey, until it becomes soft; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you below about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of a wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but to let it be, and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use warm medicines, such as warm water washes, and ointments with rose oil, and cooked washes also in warm water, and other herbs according to this method.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut it and bind it with bands, then heal it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and there is a hernia and swelling, then pierce it or cut lower; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, stop it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage for food is blocked, press down on the throat where the windpipe sits, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then compress it gently, and leave it alone for a few days, then treat it with ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then pierce it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave them until the wound drains and is cleaned out and the passage is unblocked; and if the wound is fresh, dust it with the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound, and a fistula forms, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a spear or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound breathes wind: thus you will know that the wound is mortal. And if the wound is not deep, but fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor tie it up for fear of bleeding to death, but rather let the blood flow out and return to the body, and let the patient sleep over the wound for three days or more; then spasms, tremors, and pains in the limbs will not come. And when you see good signs, you will know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal it then with poultices and other remedies until it is healed. And if it cannot heal, but suppurates, then you will know that there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, in front or behind, then cure it as one who is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has chipped pieces, then remove the wound, and draw out the splinters if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound fester, and thus lighten the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium, and small ruptures of the belly; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or nerves of the intestines protrude, causing the entrance of air; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one returns the intestines into it more with pins, when one does not return them gradually from cold to warmth; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, and return more with difficulty, and therefore the smaller wound is better, because one resets the intestines to their place more easily than with other wounds. And know that there are four types of ruptures of the belly: the two common stitches occur in the stitch of the belly, and the stitch of other wounds of the body; and the two other stitches are proper to other wounds, and yet they are more proper to the stitch of the belly, and I will say one each and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestine has come out, and there is a need to put it back in, this can be done in two ways: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water, or cook it in squinant water with cypress and spike lavender, and rose the intestine until the swelling is relieved; and sometimes doing this warming restraint, and it is helped by the sole to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling leaving, then moisten the intestine with water or old wine in which malva leaves have been cooked, for it is a remedy for constriction; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with an instrument used to treat hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than cutting, which one must not do without great need; and the instrument for splitting is: insert it into the curve and push out, and see the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines jump out, he puts them back in according to their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power, because this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs above his head; and if it is in the upper abdomen, he raises his head and feet above the lower parts, and also if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, then the injured part should be raised higher than the other. And you must manage as I say in large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have ready, then take a piece of gauze with your hand and hold it over the entire wound, and assemble the lips; and that is the common method of sewing, and it is that you pierce an needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound, then leave from the head of the wound a space of two fingers, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with both sides of the subcutaneous tissue underneath, so that you make it pierce that part, and assemble the two ends of the subcutaneous tissue together with three together; then tie the thread around the needle from both sides, then assemble the two edges of the wound evenly, and then leave a space of two fingers, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is bound; and these needles must be medium-sized, between thin and thick, because thin needles cut through all the flesh, and very thick ones cannot enter well: so they should be medium-sized; and you should not push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, so that they do not cut and open the wound before it heals; then tie the ends of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient when sleeping, and put tents or bandages on the ends of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This sewing method with needles is most suitable for small wounds, because it only requires one needle or two. The second sewings is common, and it is that you assemble the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the subcutaneous tissue together at a needle where there is a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these edges all four together, then bring the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews clothes; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a little finger; this sewing suits men, and I sewed up a wound on a man's abdomen, which had been cut with a knife, and was more than a palm wide, and the intestines were protruding by two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sutured for 15 days, and I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I applied old cotton to the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and thread it from the outside through to the inside; when it has pierced the skin directly in, then hold the end of the thread where you threaded the needle, and pierce the other side of the wound from the inside out until it reaches the outside; and the idea of this suture is that you sew just as a leather worker sews皮leather, leaving the thread on one side and pulling it tight on the other, until the whole suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes properly, is as follows: take two pieces and join them together naturally, then apply one end of the thread to the other, in such a way that you pierce one end only and leave the two ends of the wound; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside part inward to the inside, through the two ends of the wound; then pierce both ends from the outside part inward, through two other ends of the thread on the opposite side; this is the correct method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should sew the belly with two needles, with thread in each; then one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, as those who sew caries; know that when the rout is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more painful than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, so that the burn has moved, then put back the intestines and the lining; then put on the powder, charming charcoal, and if the burn has moved, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; then tie the thread, and sew up the lips and the miroach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, then put on, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need any other medicine in various situations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the principal members, then you should moisten a light lamb's wool in tempered warm oil, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the buttocks; and if there is pain or inflammation in the bowels, which often happens, then enema with tepid black wine, and likewise if the inflammation comes just to the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it's the large intestine, it's easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called 'young', cannot heal when they are raw, and it is because of the thinness of the veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of their nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.
