And if the hair jumps out of the wound, then put it back in as well as the intestines, while they are fresh; and if they are old and have become green or black, then you should tie up the area that is black so that no blood flow comes from it, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends down below the wound until the extraction is eased when the hair falls out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the wound where the boil was
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured, and the wound is small, then one can heal it in some people, for I saw that a man was pierced by a lance in the belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and was swollen and became a fistula, and from it came digestion and flatulence; I applied a poultice according to what I could, and did not stop subtilizing until it was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him stitching, I doubted that the patient had pain in his belly; and he had no pain, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a way: take fine thread from great testicles, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, put it on the two lips so that it tightens its mouth; and then tie the thread, and it will stay like that so that he cannot untie it, then put another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is all bound up; and then cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the wound is in the intestine and no harm comes to the patient, and one can sew up the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in this way: take the tip of this intestinal thread that has been well-dissected, and then tie it to the tip of a thin linen thread, and thread the needle, and sew up the wound; and this way of sewing with thread is only as strong as the way of confidence and hope; and if the wound is large and broad, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no strength or health, unless it is very thin.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is swollen and becomes bow-shaped.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the green-ness of hardened and white nodules, where there is no pain, and is bowed like the feather of a bird; and sometimes it is clear and bowed, and sometimes thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no pus, is only due to one of nine causes: namely, because of the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard matter inside it, and on the edges, which does not allow pus to form; or because there is too much swelling; or the site is damaged, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or because the region's natural disposition is slow in digestion, late in healing, and prone to inflammation; or because there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Then I shall tell you about the treatment of a fistula which is caused by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the sinus, or from the intestine, or from the bladder, or from any of the sides, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and also those that come from the primary property of the principal member, and in similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of sad healing, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is a fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it recognized, then take an iron or bronze tent, if the fistula is straight, so hold it; and if the fistula is crooked, then seek it with a тон тон of lead, for the lead bends according to the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well explore it by tents, then cleanse it through one of the openings by enema, for moisture travels from one opening to another, and cleanses; then squeeze it hard in your hand, so that you may know whether there is bone or nerve, and is deep-seated and painful, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press your hand; and when you truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then treat it according to what I have said, and remove the foulness and rotten matter within; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you must probe deeply as far as you can, then put moist tents in medicine water, and insert them into the fistula, up to its head, so that the medicine may corrode the excess which remains at the bottom; and then put healing ointments on it until it is healed, and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is damaged by the fistula, then treat it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve bothers your limbs primarily, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then treat with things that are hot until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and becomes swollen again as before, know that you have not gone deep enough: then expose and probe until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the area; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach it; then there is no other remedy except to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then extract it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose; and if there are many bones, pull them all out, leaving none behind. And if moisture causes contrary effects, and there is no error or fear, then dry and char, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something on the wound to draw out pus, and let it remain until the pus has run around the bone, and then the bones will come loose more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, then clean only the rottenness until all the blackness is gone, and then heal the wound; and if there is a large part of the bone rotten, and it comes to the bone marrow, then it must be cut away and covered completely down to the rotten part, and then healed once it has been sewn up. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help from my work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matter came out through the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and had no cause to drain pus; but the doctors, through their folly, worked on him until the abscesses opened up and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many holes appeared through which blood and moisture from the body flowed; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, so that I was called to see him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what was flowing out of the holes into a great body; and the skin of the young man became red, and had a citron color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent at one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one came against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened therefore, and probed one of the openings until I uncovered a portion of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone within; I applied what appeared to me to be medicine for the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed; and then I began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but could not close it; so I began again, and uncovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and applied medicine to it, and then removed it, and struggled to close the wound; but I was unable, because whenever I probed around a palm's width of the bone, I had to pull it clear of its socket, and then restore it with medicines; and it healed slowly, and there was no need to repeat the procedure except for the weakness of the injury, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often with the blood-letting he bled profusely, but was completely healed, and a hard lump grew in place of the bone, and he had a good disposition and no harm or contrary effect anywhere, neither when walking nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, one should treat it in this way: take a length of linen and tie it to the end of the exposed bone, and command someone to pull it upward; and put another piece of coarser linen under the first, and tie it over the lump that is above the bone, and pull on the end so that you draw out the corrupted flesh underneath, and uncover the flesh above where you see the corruption, so that the string does not cut into the flesh; and put a hot poker or a flat piece of wood underneath the bone to cover up the corrupted flesh; and one should keep pulling until one can see and feel the corruption, and do this again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place a heated iron underneath, and then sew from one side of the corruption to the other, and apply the poultice from the edge of the corruption, as we have said. And if the corruption is at the joint, then cut into the infected joint and sew up the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the area between two joints, there is no need to cut further than the joint; and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or foot, it is a difficult matter, but you must still investigate the corrosion and how it presents itself to you; then cleanse it in every way you can without damaging the vein or nerve; and know that there are many different tools for cutting into these bones, depending on their position, shape, size, thinness, and hardness. And therefore you should prepare a tool for each procedure as needed. Know that your work will show you the tool you need according to your knowledge of this art and the characteristics of the disease; then choose the tool you need accordingly.
dou feu	from fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The heads can become dislocated due to internal or external causes; and when you have treated this corrosion with remedies, and they do not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to the site of the corrosion, so that the patient escapes death by this or by the greater evil of the defect in the limb; and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if burnt by fire, and after the blackness, the corrosion spreads from limb to limb, and affects the whole body; therefore, cover it quickly, and if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures, such as sea scorpions, vipers, and similar animals, and the corrosion is on the head, then cover it and do not give it any chance to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is fatal, and there is no remedy other than reducing the amount of poison; and do the same when the corrosion affects the foot: if it affects the first joint, then cover it below the next joint; and if it affects the foot, then cover the whole foot; and if it rises into the leg, then cover it at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to tie off the affected limb with a ligature, and use a spatumile to separate the skin from the bone so that the bone is exposed; then cover it and place a linen cloth on each side so that the ligature does not touch the healthy tissue and cause further injury or abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the area gently, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete. Then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it heals. I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he developed discoloration that looked like a burn, and this corrosion started at his big toe on his foot, spreading to cover his entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he covered his foot, and it healed. A long time after, the corrosion reappeared on his finger, and he came to me, and I applied some counter-irritant substances after cleansing his body, but I could not stop the corrosions; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, for I had no hope of removing the matter by incision. I also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, as his vital forces were weak. He became desperate, returned home, covered his hand, and healed. I have told you this story so that others may learn from it and know what to do if they encounter a similar case.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess occurs in a fleshy area, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; and then it bursts and drains, and the flesh jumps, and the spot remains hollow, just like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not heal up to the bone or the nerve; and such a disease is called "sain," and is not called "fistula." But if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called a "fistula"; and the skin is such that you can cover the entire skin all around, and particularly when it is thin, just like cloth; and it does not heal over.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have reason to believe that the skin is healing and the corruption is not deep, and the flesh is thick, then treat it with a clyster as follows: examine whether the breast is swollen, and the flesh which is in it has a foul odor; then clyster it with Egyptian medicine made thus: take ash, and oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and put the medicine into a vessel over the fire, until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of it according to your need, and dissolve it in water and honey, and clyster the breast, and squeeze the opening; let it remain there for two hours, then squeeze it out; do this many times until the breast is cleansed and the pus removed; and sometimes clysters are made with water from ashes when this medicine is not available; take vinegar from grape vines, and pour water over it, then strain it, and clyster it until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or the ash-water, then clyster with water and honey in which there is a little litharge ground; or clyster with honey and wine to which has been added honey that has healing properties and washes clean, and the wine causes the wound to dry up. And when you have done this, and you see that the breast is well cleansed, then clyster it with something that will produce flesh in it; take diaphoretic plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or clyster with some medicines and ointments of which I have spoken in the section on ointments. And if the opening to the breast is small and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it with a little iron, and put in some tent of the Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is very large, then cut away and leave only the part where the clyster can enter, and if the opening that drains the pus is above, then cover it or cover it lower down.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are full, do not allow any charing; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, arrange things so that the bowels move to the lowest place they can, for when the bowels are full, do not allow any charing, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, arrange things so that the bowels move slightly downward, and leave nothing of the bowels; and take consolidative medicines to put over the wound, and let them be on the linen drape that covers the entire wound; then cover the most forceful place of the breast opening more widely than before, then apply a soothing ointment over the other drape according to the quantity of the opening, and place it over the wound opening to ease the bowels, and do not remove the large drape except after many days once; and that which is over the breast opening, remove often to remove the bowels, and know what comes from the bowels, whether venom or pus or a little or a lot, or digested or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that rises over the wound opening, then know that the breast is healing, and approach the wound; and then loosen it in the morning, or at noon, and when you loosen the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if breast milk flows crookedly after many days, know that the breast will not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread over a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people who have long-term injuries to their flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite; and if indigested food vomits from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not cured; and if the breast is slow to heal, and is distant, then apply dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in nature, like diafanit ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and it is the best medicine. Take diafanit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and arose from old wine, equal in substance; then cook it and use it. And the same is done with thickened honey when diafanit ointments are not available; take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them into powder over the honey while it is on the fire; then glue a cloth to it, and apply it to the breast, and sometimes aristologus, a long-root herb, is administered, as well as roots of the celestial lily, which is like flour made from beans and centaury. Use simple or compound remedies: grind them into powder, and apply them to the honey I mentioned, and use it. And if the cure is prolonged, and not healed by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep, and it causes impression in the bone, or in the hard limbs, or in the soft tissues; so the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the thumb or other fingers, or it may appear on other parts of the body; and when it becomes infected and goes untreated, an abscess forms, and it grows and discharges pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it affects the entire nail. The corrosion extends to the bone, causing a putrid pain, and the affected digit swells and turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut away all the dead tissue remaining under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; but if the nail becomes infected and begins to push out the dead tissue, and the wound starts to bleed, then you should place a thread under the nail to draw out the dead tissue, and then cut it away gently and carefully. Put strong medicines on the remaining tissue to remove it all, and then treat the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it and draw it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone being corrupted, cut it at the knuckle of the finger as it is said above, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is swollen and painful, one must first heal it; then cut the fingernail of the spatulile obliquely from above, and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain should be dulled in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two toenails that grow on some people's feet by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is bone in them, and sometimes they have nails, and some grow at the root of the toe joint, or the growth is in some knuckle of the toe.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in the nostril of the right side does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the right side, by chance moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is light, in such a way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is painful to cure; keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born in the nostril of the left side, you must first cut the flesh roundly up to the bone, then cut the bone with a convenient silk for this, then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The dislocation of two bones together occurs through birth, or the sudden impact of a wound, or the scalding of fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary to cut this suture so that the nostrils repair according to their natural forms; then place between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil so that they do not stick together; or place between two pieces of thin lead, until the slits are closed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the glue comes to either of his hands with the palm, then cover the glue as it should be.
des vils	of the wicked
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large vessels filled with melancholy superfluities that affect many parts of the body; and they are more common in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him some purgative medicine sometimes, and then heal the wound with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	There are two types of treatment for varicose veins: one is to cut them and draw out the black blood; the other is to tie off the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The procedure for phlebitis is as follows: first, soak the leg in very hot water until the veins are dilated, then compress the leg from above the thigh to below the knee; next, cut the vein in one or more places with a wide incision, then draw out and drain the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood as the patient can tolerate is withdrawn; then ligate the vein and have the patient apply a poultice of gall-nut and black hellebore; when the veins fill again, repeat the evacuation and bleeding.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment for this condition is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you don't have a bath, heat it over a fire, and then press on the vein from the long end towards the knee, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin at the nail, and scrape the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord; then tie the thread under, so that it is raised from the skin, and then tie it gently at the nail, as before; then make another cut, or several if necessary, then raise and tie it at the toe, then pull and raise it to the second cut; then pull it out from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then tie it off; and if you cannot pull and raise it, then insert a strong double thread with a needle, and tie and pull it, and tie it under the thread, and turn your hand from side to side so that it comes out; and be careful not to cut it, because if it cuts, then it cannot be pulled and raised, and it brings harm to the patient; and when you have fully treated it, then place moist wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the wound site; and dress it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to cover a vein is curved, and does not cut so that it covers the vein; and it should be a large curve because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of a civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is winded in the legs, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in land where there is no moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pustules that come under the skin, as do snakes and worms, winding between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that there comes a great swelling in the leg, then the place changes, and the wound starts to come out, as well as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder opens, you should wrap a piece of cloth around it, from three and a half inches to four inches, and tie it, and leave the cloth hanging on the leg, and every time that some comes out, wrap the cloth around it; and if it is too long, cut off part of it and wrap the remaining part, and do not cover it at its root as long as it all comes out. And if you cover it, it goes back into the flesh, and makes an abscess and swelling in that place, and a serious illness; because of this, it should be treated little by little until it is all gone, and nothing remains in the body. Sometimes this wound is treated when it is five or ten inches long, and once a man came to me whose was twenty inches long; and when you cover it, put in a reed or tube, and pierce it to the bottom so that everything comes out, and empty the matter inside that causes disease, then treat the place with healing medicines for a few days, and then cure it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein bleeds profusely, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and a lot of pus comes out, and from which it rains; therefore treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cattle, and it is caused by a small worm that grows between the skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and emerges; and it is caused by the putrefaction of some humors, just as worms, snakes, and roundworms grow in the belly. And one fears its malice, for when it moves through the body and ascends to the head, it can enter and destroy the eye; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn out, it cannot be helped except when it is cut: so you must therefore tie the place above and below with a strong string tightly, then cut on top of it and draw it out forcefully; and if the pus runs deep into the flesh, and you do not draw it out, cauterize it with fire on top until it comes out; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near to the eye, then tightly constrict under it with a forceps, then cut on top of it and draw it out forcefully; and one should use the cleansing of the body with medicated solutions for the evil humors, and with poultices of warm meats for pustules.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and a little while after, I saw it rise up like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another. The pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran throughout her body until it came to the other arm; then she said that she felt it turning around her body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this illness in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have often seen pain move from one place to another, but not as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and their veins are uncovered, and thus appears this compelled windiness; and it does not appear according to this reason for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then lie above and below, and then press on top until that windiness forced out of place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat with that which expels windiness, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some with large points, and small, and forked, and soldered; and some with two angles, and those with tongues, and some have parts; and they split in a member in two ways: either in a principal member they split, like brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into any part of these limbs and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears to you: then you must be careful about removing this arrow, because death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	The sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces the bone and passes through the skull, and there is a discharge from the brain which is on top of the skull, and there is redness and swelling all around, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of blood; and perhaps fluid flows out of the nose or ears; and he might lose his speech and voice; and there is white moisture coming out of the wound like pus, and also like a bruise on meat; and if this sign appears to you, then cease the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not embedded in him.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of jaundice when it affects the body are that it is located near the left breast, and feels as though it has been pierced with a sharp object, and is not hollow; and sometimes the jaundice makes the patient mute, and black blood comes out, and there is a feeling of coldness and cold sweat, and a fainting: then know without doubt that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of pleurisy that affects the lungs is that without pain foam comes out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if an arrow pierces the sole of the foot, it is near the small bones; and it causes great pain and great distress and sighing; and all the shoulder joints move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food might escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the belly, and no feces escape through the bowel, then there is little hope of a cure, nor of extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine escapes and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and leg, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	A certain person had an arrow that struck him in the jaw at the root of his teeth; I treated it, and pulled it out from under the flesh of his ear, and he was healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I treated an arrow that struck him in the fat of his eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was lodged there, and only the tip could be seen pointing towards the mouth; the arrow was as large as a Turkish bowstring, with its entire shaft light-colored without ears; he was healed and no bad accidents came to him.And I treated an arrow that struck him in the fat of his eye under the eyelid, and the arrow was lodged there, and only the tip could be seen pointing towards the mouth; the arrow was as large as a Turkish bowstring, with its entire shaft light-colored without ears; he was healed and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic, to the ears; I soothed the pain, and extracted it with skill, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I also extracted an arrow from a man's home, which had pierced his belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days passed, his condition did not improve; so I cut into the arrow, and removed it, and he suffered no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow in his back, and the wound has healed over it; and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural habits, nor suffers any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it remained there without causing him great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And drew an arrow from the home of the prince the king, who had it lodged in his head, and it was a little declined to the right side; and the arrow was all drawn out I was called to the cure after it was drawn three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with a sharp probe, and did not feel anything; but he felt numbness and pain under his right ear.Apres qu’el fu tuit traïe, il me demanda la cure del soun mal de dent, car il sentoit une gran dolor a sa dent, et adonques convint il que je remuassies la dent del soun mal.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	After it was all drawn out, he asked me to treat his toothache because he felt great pain in his tooth; so I decided to move the tooth of its ailment.I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.I applied an astringent and digestive poultice to the area, so that the swelling would go down; and the mark of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the ointment several times, and the wound healed immediately, and the patient suffered for a long time, feeling the arrow in his nose; he told me so himself.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound several times until it healed, and I tested it, feeling the head of the arrow which was sticking out; then I adjusted the opening of the wound with the same medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared clearly; after about four months, the wound closed up completely, but then it burst open again; so I continued to probe and manipulate it with various instruments, until one day I was able to grab hold of the arrowhead with some specially made forceps, as described later in this chapter, and I drew it out; thus I treated the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctors judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it therefore, and the wound was sewed up, and the patient entirely recovered.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may make your own remedy of what I do not say, for books cannot embrace everything; but wise masters compare things based on a little knowledge, and on what is present and lacking, they find new remedies and new instruments, through the descent of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows strike the limbs where they are pierced in two ways: either through the place where they enter or through another part; and those which go out through where they entered are called intranasal arrows, and sometimes they come out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it be until the carcass is putrefied all around, and let the outlet be relieved; and likewise, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it be for some days, and move it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce all around with a very thin stick until the opening around is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not pull it out, but let it be until it is even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the cortex, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck in the bone only, and does not reach the cortex, and the patient remains for several days without a bad accident, then treat it with the method of pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck very tightly and cannot come out, then administer cuts around it, as I have told you; then cure the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged in the body so that it cannot be seen, then seek it throughout the entire body; and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then cut open the wound so that it is large enough for you to pull out the arrow; and if there are barbs on the arrowhead that are preventing its removal, then remove the flesh that is caught on them from both sides as much as you can, and then bend or fold back the barbs so that you can extract the arrow; be careful not to break the arrow shaft as you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then let it lie until around the nail is soft, then pull it, for the extraction is eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood is contrary to what you expect, then refer to what we have said about treating an arrow wound in its chapter; and be careful to avoid cutting into any nerves or veins, and use every means possible to draw out the arrow safely, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently, according to the patient's condition; and reset the dislocated joint according to how it was before the arrow struck, for that is the greatest help you can give, and if you cannot do so, then set it as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Arrows that come from elsewhere, or where something protrudes from them, or the skin is swollen in that area, whether one sees or feels it clearly: cut above it, as high as the pincers can reach, and then pull it out; if it flies out at once, so much the better.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand around, as deep as it can go into the bone, and widen the wound, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now and try pulling again until it comes out; and if the arrow is inside, push it all the way in; and if the arrow is short, and you see fit to administer pressure, then press the instrument into the arrowhead so that the point of the arrow goes into the instrument; then pull it out, and if the arrow is stuck, push the instrument in with its point entering inside to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is pierced, you should cut around the flesh where the venom is, as much as you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is in the thigh or buttock or belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close by, and you can reach it; and you must be careful not to touch the vein and nerve, and then pull it out, and then close the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the feathered end is like the feathers of a bird, to push against the point of the arrow, as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tongs for pushing and gripping is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one can be bled, and in the head there are XVI of these, namely: two veins located behind the ears, called 'herbech'; and two arteries in the temples that are visible; and two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, called 'aspires'; and one vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two windpipes that are in the neck; and two veins that are above the lips, these are the veins called 'augeherich'; and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.
