The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the rib cage, and the common people call it 'vein of the head'; and the middle one is called 'fast', and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it 'vein of the heart'; and the basilic is on the right side of the rib cage, and the common people call it 'vein of the belly', and it is above the pudenda, and it is that one from which they bleed, which clearly opens above the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvator is the vein between the auricular and annular, and it has two branches; and in the leg and the foot there are three veins: one is under the curve of the groin on the left side of the rib cage, and the second is below the ankle on the right side; and the vein called 'thigh', which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are after the ears aids ancient cataracts and emigration; and the qualities of the bloodletting, as I told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then wring the patient's neck with a rope, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head: press them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, sign it; then take the lance, and pierce it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein upstream, and pierce both skin and vein thoroughly for a distance of two fingers, and let the blood come out until you see it; then stop it and ligature it, so that it is healed; and I have already said about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries in the temples is good for old migraines, and for sore eyes and habitual ophthalmia, and for agues affecting the eye sockets; and the qualities of the bloodletting are as I have said: and it is that the patient strains his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible; and he feels the pulse under his finger, and then he signs with his finger; then he lifts the vein at the top of his finger, and inserts the lance underneath, and lifts the vein at the top, and cups it, as you have done in the other veins, and lets the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and their release at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as beneficial as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for diseases of the face that are old and have migrated, and have become red; and its qualities are such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point over the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see; then loosen the neck of the patient, and tie the vein until it is healthy, and sometimes the work is done with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and it heals crookedly, because the bone is close by, and perhaps breaks the flame when it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins that are in the temples helps with eye diseases, and redness, and red eyes, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting one or both ears, as before; then he bleeds, and the bleeding should be through the vein, a little from the long flame, a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps it will break; then blood will flow, as much as you need, and then tie it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein by the nose is good for ague, and for sudden fever, and for diseases of the face, such as swelling and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient should pinch his nose, then squeeze his nostrils with his left hand, and take a long, thin flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it off for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two sinuses also helps with strangulation of the windpipe, and the beginning of hoarseness, and many diseases, and empyema, and corroding sores, and herpes, and stomach ulcers; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient should pinch his nose as we have said; and let the healer stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein on the side a little widely, then draw the blood gently, or as much as is needed; then do the same on the other side, then untie the ligature, and gently squeeze both veins so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until the morning, so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of veins on the lips helps with sores in the mouth, and gum decay, and splitting of the lips, and toothache and gum pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit facing you, and hold his head as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being dark in color, and because there are fine dark veins around them: grab both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you doubt which they are, then grab the largest of each side, and likewise do this with the two veins above and below, for it is the same procedure.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that are beneath the tongue is aided after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is done by constricting the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient should sit between your hands in front of the sun, and you should lift up his tongue and look beneath on each side for a black vein: therefore, bleed both sides, and do not go too deep, because underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either with a large, pointed, mirting-flame, or with a subtle olive-colored needle, as you would with an eye, and they are called "anesil"; and they are large or subtle according to the size and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame of myrrh is highly renowned, and it is broad as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth and filled with thick blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	is more pointed and is for bleeding the veins, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, aids diseases that are beneath the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is fitting for the surgeon to bleed profusely, and to compress the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he compresses the artery, and bleeding comes, then it must be staunched, as I have said; and the flame should not be piercing, but cutting like a chisel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic does not open plainly, then you must stretch it and change to another; or you can take some from it, or you can bleed in its place in the arm: it opens plainly; and stop the flame with a chisel, as we have said.Et si la voinne que sainnes ne s’esgoutte pas par li flaime anesil, si covient que tu l’esgoutes par auter fleche, ou par altra maniere, si com nos avons dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mas taillans si com anesil.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the bleeding, you must stretch out the arm so that you can feel the pulse; then sign the spot with your fingernail, and then tie the arm, and cover the vein with a flame until it is numbed; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the spot puff up, for that is the artery: therefore avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bubbling up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is the artery: therefore hurry, and place your finger over it for a long time, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops; tie the arm, and leave it alone, and do not move the patient; and let him be fearful, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and he faints, and medicine is not at hand, then press on the artery until it stops, for that is where the blood flows from; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a sliver of wood from a tree branch, split it in two and take one half and bind it well until the next day; if there is no bleeding then that is good; but if not then stop the bleeding as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; the stopping of bleeding is not difficult for various wounds in this small area, nor for the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The wound in the middle if it is bleeding from above the head and below the body, because it is made of basil and cedar as we have said; and the bandage should be applied to the nerve below, and if it is too deep, and the nerve is found and inflammation and the wound is infected, and it may not heal; and this nerve often opens up in some people due to its subtlety, and if it does not open for anyone then you should treat it with an anesthetic instrument.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they should cut it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the head if it helps, that it draws blood from the brain, and helps the eyes; and one should bleed using a flame olive or myrtle, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one should seek the lightest spot, and if one misses the first time, try again; and perhaps the spots will swell in some men, if they miss the first time, but it causes no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of healing depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is done only to maintain health and prevent diseases; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins: the head, the arm, or the leg; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of digestion are apparent; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a set time, but when there is need, day or night, at all hours and all times; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women who are pregnant beyond the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	No one should bleed those who are older than sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to bleed, in any way, they should first clear the intestines with a gentle enema if they have much retained feces so that the veins do not draw harmful surplus fluids from the intestines into the principal limbs; one should not bleed those who are bloated from food, nor those who are intoxicated, as long as it has been, nor the sickly; and if one bleeds after a colic attack, vomiting, and diarrhea, and excessive sexual intercourse with a woman, and exertion, waking and fasting, and that which comes from all bodily fluids, or by weapon or from the body; then gently withdraw the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing else will cleanse the blood, to gently cleanse the blood, and one should bleed near the navel around the third hour, as we have said; and one should abstain that day from exertion, and from pinching and luxury, and similar things; and be calm and cheerful, and the bleeder should be higher than the person being bled, and he should rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature gently above the vein, for if it is too tight or too loose, it will not draw the blood; then he should rub the site with his hand until the veins swell, and one feels them; then he should moisten the blade of the bleed with a little old oil, then press his left index finger on that vein below the bleeding site, where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not break away from the blade.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Because there are veins that flow like cords to the wound, and some that are full of windiness, so that when one applies a flame, it retreats from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those; and if one opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary for the surgeon to be skilled in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, open it again a little lower down or up above, depending on which way the vein is going, if the skin is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the wound is swollen and the patient is afraid, let him go for a day or two without binding his arm; perhaps hot abscesses will form; do not enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if she wishes; and if the hole is small, pierce it with a thin needle and you fear that not as much blood flows as you wish, then apply the flame directly to that very hole; and work gently, so that the wound is swollen; because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the vein swollen, do not re-bandage it, and put a little liniment of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the liniment of oil is effective; and likewise apply the liniment of oil to every vein that you open, to stop the flow of blood; and it also acts as a poultice and bandage when applied to the site. It subsides gently when it is too swollen.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there is a large abscess that occurs often, especially when the opening of the vein is small, be quick and apply to the site a sponge moistened with warm water, and hold it for an hour; and you should do this after the flow of blood from the vein has ceased, and if a darkness or greenness remains in the area for some days, it will not harm him; and if you see anything, apply something made from aloe or myrrh dissolved in wine or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances arise from the bleeding of the basilic vein; therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the touch, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting anything we have mentioned on it, however, for it might come from an artery; instead, make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat the wound with another treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its nature and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the pus is black, let it flow out until it turns red; and if you see it is thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, to make the wound larger, and the cuts wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and let them be bled a little and often, and they should be bled by cutting diagonally, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding prevents the flow of blood and the damage to nerves, and is better than bleeding from a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is fitting to give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, let them eat moist bread three or four times before the bleeding. And if their complexion is cold, let them eat moist bread with syrup of myrrh, or with aromatic honey syrup seasoned with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cardamom, and perfumed syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he faints during bleeding, after a great deal of blood has been let, then he should inhale the vapor of a hot drink, and use aromatic syrups, and employ other remedies that we have mentioned in the chapter on syncope, to open the veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, when it is weakened by heavy bleeding, he should bleed slowly according to the amount of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to open his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong pulse, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, let him bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a great deal of blood inside the body that has been heated and causes fever; so one must draw off a large quantity, and dilate the opening until it bleeds freely; then you should attend to all the details of bleeding, and put your hand over his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come in the place of fainting, and this happens many times when the person bleeding is negligent; nor, when you see the arm loosening and bleeding a second time, and the opening closed, should you press down hard upon it; nor if it is crooked, should he stretch out his arm violently, for that would be bad; but let him keep it still while he bleeds a second time; or else put the tip of the cautery to the opening, so that the blood which is congealed at the opening of the vein may issue forth, and put some salt dissolved in water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not bind it, until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then let him bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	Veins in the arm are healthy at the site of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the bleeding is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the vein turns red; then let it be bound gently so that the vein appears well, then bleed it from the middle, not from the broad or long part; and let the opening be wide, and let the bleeding be done near the joint of the hand, and if no blood comes out, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is in winter, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it will be put in hotter water than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bleeding of the savable vein of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: stretch out the hand and put it in hot water until the vein swells; then bleed it from the side, and if you close it completely at both ends, it will do no harm; and do not go too deep, for the nerves are naked underneath the flesh. Then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled as much as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to close it up, and do the same for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The surgery of the left hand is similar to that of the right hand, and you should do everything as I told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The remedy of the sop is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the stomach, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the intestines, and the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its remedy are such that the patient should put his foot in hot water, and rub on the vein until it bursts, and apply it to the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot there goes a great deal of rain; heal it therefore at the widest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then guard against the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as well as up and down; and let the flames be anointed.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the remedy does not work the first time, try it a second time higher up, for the place is salty; do not be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and likewise make the remedy on the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its treatment helps with hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its healing is that the patient enters the bath, and twists above the ankle three times, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cover it, for the place is safe, and it is very relaxed in many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not believe this, then heal a vein on his back that opens near the little toe, and move towards the small toe, and beware of the nerves; and make the blood flow until you see it, and then untie the ligature, and place cotton over it and bind it; now it is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and bleeding is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping, which is done without fire, is done in two ways: sometimes with all fire, sometimes without; and the cupping that is done by heat and by bloodletting is performed in 14 places on the body, one of which is at the top of the head; another in the neck; two others on both sides of the neck; one under the chin; one on each shoulder; one above the hips; one on each arm; one on each leg; and one on each ankle. And cupping does not draw blood, except from small veins that are dispersed throughout the flesh, and because of this it weakens nothing at all, as is done with vein-opening; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if for the necessity of illnesses one must vomit, or due to habits, we should induce vomiting every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at all times; for there are those who, when they need to vomit, have a heavy head; and there are those who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are those who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and taste blood; and there are those who dream, and see by night blood and wounds and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is in the middle of the month, we command him to be bled after three hours of day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The mucus of the nose helps with headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it must not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this ventilation is in the place of the cerebral mucus, and it must not be used by those who are of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm; and for this reason the elderly should not use it, nor those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become oblivous, and because of this, the leech must place the cupping jar a little lower down to avoid oblivousness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventosation in the neck is located at the junction of the head and the basilic vein, and because of this, it helps with discomfort in the feet, and with fissures in the channels of the lungs, and with constipation and bloating; and one must not push on it too much, for if it is pressed too firmly, it can cause harm to the intestines, stomach, and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosations at the two sides of the neck help with headaches, and eye pain and inflammation, and with strangulation, and with toothache, and are located at the junction of the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand while placing it, so that he does not compress the artery and cause a bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and for gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is located in the area of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are effective for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventosations in the armpits are like three veins in the arm, for they attract blood from these large veins; and command the surgeon not to press too deeply, for the area is naked of flesh, and beneath it lie nerves and arteries.Li ventosation dou costel dou coté droit est en leu de la sainie de la veine dou col, et si vaut a dolors des coutes et des coutes, et as dolors des membres sus le costel; et covient qu’il ne fie mie trop em parfond, car li leus est nus.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids and diseases below, and it must be a large one made of copper, which needs to be carefully handled; otherwise, if it were thin, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal quickly, as they attract blood from throughout the body and are beneficial for old pains in the joints, the hips, and the bladder, and bring relief to flowers; they are placed at the inside of the thighs and ankles, and even though they weaken the body after prolonged use, they bring relief in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of placing the cupping glass is to first put it on empty, then suck gently, place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area turn red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then pause, remove the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those with thin skin and large pores: therefore, one should suck only once, and make wide and somewhat deep wounds, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to suck twice: the first time to make the path for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it must be pricked a third time; and when we want to draw a little blood, we only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we suck often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce it with a needle, and the end is that the veins are pierced suddenly, and it is convenient for those who have thick and hard skin, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the places of the cupping glasses with an astringent and dissolving oil: if it is in the summer, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with squash seed oil; and if it is in the winter, with watercress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or oil of aniseed, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those whom we heal have soft flesh and wide pores, no oil should be put on them, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or squash water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from bed, or water of myrrh, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large sores heal them with old wine, or with water of vinegar, or with a decoction of anise or camomile, or other similar things; and one should not bleed with a cupping glass before the bath nor in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep after being bled, but they should keep watch, when they are to be bled and when they have been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the person being bled is choleric, and if their blood is too sharp and inflamed; they should eat cool things such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar foods; and they should not eat pungent foods, or meat that is lean, nor any moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those of cold complexion should drink syrup of honey, and moderate old and new sweet wine, and eat light food, and eat pungent foods and pigeons and small birds; and the day they are bled, they should drink more than eat; and it is good to give some men triacle or musk before bleeding, or afterwards, to strengthen the main organs; and the blood should be mild, but those of hot temperament should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are applied without breaking the skin are those that are applied to the liver, and to the mumps, and to the gout, and to the belly, and the groin, and the flanks, because these members do not bear being hurt on their own, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we do when we put them on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in a member, as we do when we put cupping glasses on the belly and on the groin to reduce a swollen member; and it removes pain when there is gangrene or stone, and by its attractive power it may draw out the gangrene, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it acts when one applies it to the liver and to the mumps when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty merely to suck; and sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it is two digits wide and half a palm deep, and on the side around the middle there is a small hole, like that for an awl, and it should be of brass, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of brass or iron, to place a candle, and they are both large and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this ventouse on the limb: take the candle of wax or the linen, and place it within the ventouse at the crossbar in the middle, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then place it on the limb, and hold your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor will go out, and one removes the ventouse. Then take the linen as before, and repeat often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass therefore which is administered for sickness of pleurisy, has no rod nor hole, and is not removed until when it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only by itself; and that is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not removed until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in naked flesh, such as fingers or toes, and others; and the quality of using them is that when you find leeches which are in sweet waters without burrowing, take them; and put them into sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let it be bled from a vein and cupped, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the leeches upon it; and when they are full and crawl away, if it is a place where one can place a cupping glass, then put one on, for that is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the area with ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the veins are too tight after the body of the leeches, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the leeches are engorged; and if the veins are multiplied, then place crushed vitriol, or gales, and similar things on top, until they are stopped; or you place half a handful of peeled peas on the area and leave them until they turn black at the site, and it will now stop; and if you need more, then take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the area with fresh blood, or you pierce it with a needle until the vein flows, and then place the leeches on top; and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach themselves; and when you see that they are defecating, then powder over some crushed aloe, or ash, and they will now cling.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people who delve into this chapter have never seen any of the ancient books or read any letters; and for this reason, knowledge is stranger in our land, for I have never found anyone good at it; and I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired the science, and through experimentation and the habit of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought in, just as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the matters and the chapters, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when any bruising or dislocation or twisting or fracture occurs in someone, you must hurry to heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or youth, or old age; and if the weather is not very hot or too cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cold meats, and deer and hare meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill themselves with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have reason to suspect a hot abscess or swelling of matter in the limb; then let the patient return to their first treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, then one should nourish the patient with foods that promote swelling or粘稠度(viscosity), such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, feet, pig's stomach, ox's maw, fresh fish, and full-bodied wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the body swells more quickly with moisture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well set or joined according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, as in the bones of small children; but have no concern, reset the broken bone with the large tendons that stretch and join the limb together, as it was before; and do not stop at all in his work, and for this he should eat plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a break that goes to the root, and another in sharpening, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break throughout a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own technique and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes back in its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it appears well through deformation, and it sounds when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or pain in the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can still have twisting, or splintering, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come below, and then hold it firmly and gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that the fracture which goes into the bone, and where the two parts are separated, they must now be put back together evenly, so that the abscesses heal; and if hot abscesses appear, then let it be for a day, until the abscesses are calm; then put it back to the way it was, as easily and gently as you can, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of one where there are pieces missing; then bind it, as is appropriate afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or your hand if it is a small member, or by two tendons, or by one tendon and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are separated, then bring them together by all means in their places as you can, and be careful that by your work there does not come injury or pain to the patient; and join well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand whether it seems well or not; then adjust it nicely, and do not strain it too much or press it as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is ready, then carefully treat the patient so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or otherwise; and be sure that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, then it is not yet healed, and you should put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is set straight, so that no crookedness comes to it when it is healed; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken bones are diverse in size, length, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: these should be wrapped with soft, fine linen; and for larger ones, such as thigh and leg: use a wide, strong bandage, for the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb and constrict it evenly all around, so that no swelling remains; then wrap light sponges all around, three or four times according to the size of the limb, and tighten your hand a little at every turn of the bandage, then go over the broken part and tighten less, so that the break is moved away a little; and soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp most of the healthy part, then take another bandage and wind it straight around the broken part again; then go back to the part underneath the break, and tighten gently, neither too tight nor too loose, as we have said above in the first hour; then put between the bandages sponges of linen or cloth, until they are all even, then bind all over with a bandage, and then put on your splints well-made, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing and hot upon the abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it thus for a few days; then press gently with your fingers, and they should be made of half a rod of willow, or of wood used for making knives, or of palm branches, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the finger that is placed on the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as the limb requires in terms of smallness or size; then press gently with your fingers just as you did at first, then tie a thread over them properly, just as in the case of the first fracture; the tighter it is, the better; and the thread must be thin, neither too thick nor too thin, and it should be made of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen foolish people do when they make their knots with twisted cords, and this is a great error, for the knot cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should be no less than two fingers between each finger.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore under the eyes after the dislocation in their healthy state, then place beneath them linseed poultices or soft lambswool so that it does not break.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture and the vein is broken, I will describe its treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you shall know that it is not right to pull out all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, it should not be bandaged for more than five or seven days, or longer according to the security of the hot abscess; and here is the manner of the ancient plaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take flour from the walls of the mill, and cook it with an abundance of egg, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way to heal fractures in various situations, especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster that restores broken bones and dislocation and torsion: take 3 grams of absinthe, and ladani, and enule, and asafoetida, and gum arabic, and mastic, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 5 grams; alechimic 8 grams. Make these into a powder and mix them with plenty of eggs; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and it is useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for twisting: take mugwort and mallow, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 8 grams; acacia 6 grams; Armenian bole 10 grams, and grind well, and cook with water or an abundance of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones that have been dislodged from their places, and to ease the resulting pain, and for fractures: take new lamb's wool, and soak it in lard and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and alleviating pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earthworm leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster from them.
