Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster to help heal a fracture and reduce swelling from an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, camomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, one part each; and grind them, and cook with wine. If the affected member is swollen, cook it with moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another, stronger method of plaster for when a tough abscess occurs during healing.Take the root of marshmallow, camomile, and violet flowers, one part each; and grind them, and cook with wine. If the affected member is swollen, cook it with moist coriander water or water, and apply it.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of viscum album, and flax seed, buckthorn, camomile, and marigold, and violets, of each one part; and grind them, and cook with salt water, or fresh water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrites says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to restore it except for cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on a broken member, to restore it, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and lamb's tail, or owl feathers, and viscumsalve, and salt equally, and bruise them, and make plaster and lie in it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor move the bone from its place; if not, loosen it by hand for several days. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take light cloth, and sponge of the sea moistened in water, and apply to the area until the itching ceases and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then apply a poultice of linseed oil and vinegar, and bind it with a nut, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain be removed, then begin gently again, and a little plaster, and do not pull it as hard as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, take it all out, and you need to apply a poultice and a bandage, and do this again as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb does not receive anything of what we have said, do not dislocate it until three, four, five or seven days have passed; and sometimes let it be for twenty days, according to what one sees, as long as the fracture remains, and the adjustment of the flesh above approaches; then restrain it more than before, and increase its meat, as I have said before; and if you see the place drier than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; therefore moisten it with warm water, every time you dislocate it, and this should be every third day, and loosen a little the bandage; through this work, nourishment reaches the limb, and quickly heals what the foolish healers do, who restore the limb crookedly: this is bad, and such work is cowardly, and I see nothing in it but weariness and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with different shapes and distinct causes. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the bone all the way to the syrinx, which is under the bone, as with an axe or a club. This type of fracture is called "axe fracture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a closed fracture, or a split, or from the impact of stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which approaches the membrane below the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is in the bone as thin as a hair, and the split is small, then this type of fracture is called "capillary". And if the wound is made by stone or by falling, or by something similar, and drives the piece of bone inward, and the spot is chapped like the way blacksmiths work on kettles; then the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more often in those with moist bones at the top, like the head of a child; and it happens with all types of fractures where small pieces are dispersed like pebbles; I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaking by examination, and by corruption of the flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is discovered when one uncovers the bone and rubs it, then the black crack becomes visible.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be aware of accidental illnesses, and if you see any harmful events such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, palpitations, fever, eyes popping out and turning red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a surprising accident and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, then you must hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the membrane under the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents we have described do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part thus: and it is necessary that you grasp the head of the injured person, and expose the bone in every way that you can, and the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs on exposing the bone, or a hot abscess, use aid as appropriate, and you must fill the site with wet rags soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the hot abscesses are calmed, and be sure there is no more bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of treatment: one method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he puts in another stitch larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you should have various different stitches, some narrow and some wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work quickly so that you do not pierce the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, then you should pierce it all around, so that you can use stitches with awls, not going deeper than the bone of the skull; and it must have a rim or circle on top so that the point does not go beyond the bone. You should have several of these so that each one goes into the thickness of the bone, and you will need awls for all parts of the skull. There are three types of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is to place an awl on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the awl to another place a little later, and continue all around. Then use the chisels to chip away at the space between the fragments of bone, doing this as skillfully and gently as you can, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you are using, like tweezers or pincers; be careful not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is appropriate to resect the membrane that clings to the bone with any other similar instrument to an incisive forceps, but it should be more slender and more delicate than other forceps; and if anything remains of the small bones or scales, remove them lightly with the instrument; then cure the wound with tenting and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of doing it which is safer, according to Galen, who praised it highly, is as follows:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the broken bone is visible, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place under the head of this incisor, a lenticular shape, which is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sore on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet above, so that you lightly strike the bone all around, and be very careful of the membrane that is underneath; if it is adherent to the bone, then loosen it lightly, for one can loosen it well without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then one must smooth that roughness, and remove the shards with a very thin rasp, of which you should have various sizes, in order to apply the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take first a large rasp, and then a finer one, and do not cease doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and subtle breaks, you must minister according to its nature; and this is not answered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, you should take a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three layers, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not burden the sinus, then administer another bandage above, and do not tighten it more than is necessary to hold the wound; leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscesses are soothed, then loosen it, and apply medicine such as roots of lilies, and flour of beans, and incense powder, and aristologus, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it over the wound, and administer medicine without biting; and be careful that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow any pus to collect, for when pus collects on the membrane of the brain, it hardens and becomes infected, causing great harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no evil accident happens to the patient as we have said, for it is certain without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness comes only because of the medicine that has been applied, how effective it is, then you should take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue a bandage to it, and place it on the syphilitic sore; then cure it in ways that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the upper jaw are broken, one alone or both, for they are two bones; and the one underneath is cartilaginous, and does not break but only dislocates or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should boil your little finger or a needle, and place that broken part inside your index finger, and hold it in place with your thumb, until the nail regrows according to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and you cannot reach it with your fingers, you should place it at the end of a thick piece of wood.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do likewise, and try to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the wounds are healed, then boil some linen bandages at the tip of the nail, if the break is in one part.Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et mette un petus dedens la brisure, et en une partie d’une cotte, et le chief dou neis en l’autre, et li neis entremil, et fai li petuz tan estreins qu’il tene li II pars de la brisure, et li cotte tan lons qu’il tene les II pars entremiles; et metteli sus li neis, si le petus dedens la brisure, et li cotte entremiles.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you tie one to each side of the bone, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so large that they fill the holes in the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must moisten the tents with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but one should moisten the tent with egg white and flour; then leave it until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes we put goose feathers in the wound instead of tenting, and then a thin cloth around it, and holds the fracture in place, and blows the patient's breath among them; now do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if warm abscesses arise in the nose while you are working on it, then put on cerate or cotton wetted in rose oil, or a little diaquillon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hard abscess comes, put on a plaster made from flour of fine wheat and powdered incense, cooked with egg white, then apply it over light dressings and do not tie the nail; and if the fracture in the nail is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, extract it using suitable instruments for that purpose, then clean the wound and treat it with healing poultices and ointments, and if there is no wound inside the nail, treat it with tent dressings and apply splints until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below, and there is no external wound, and the joint is only slightly displaced without any fracture in the bone, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should insert your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the dislocation is on the left side of the jaw, then use the right index finger of the other hand, and gently push it into the dislocation and pull outward with the other hand, keeping the pressure equal on both sides.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer an extension of two parts until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or dislocation, then bind them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and then place ceratum on the broken jaw, and lay upon it a double cloth; and place upon the cloth a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather the same size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it onto the face as tightly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and to eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it after three days, and then reset it to its original position; and apply a poultice over it of powder from the mill with an egg or flour of chickpeas, after you have removed the ceratum; and place over the poultice a light layer of lamb's wool, and if the poultice becomes hot, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; often it is healed within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the jaw is dislocated due to moisture, then you must loosen and reset it, and instruct the patient not to move his jaw; and place over it light lamb's wool; and if you see that it is becoming dislocated, then place over it a piece of leather, or a small cloth, or lamb's wool, and the splint, and the ceratum, and the poultice, according to what is needed.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine whether any piece of the bone has been removed; then remove it subtly with appropriate instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, then close the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it an appropriate poultice to encourage flesh growth, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the scrotum
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The collarbone breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: it can be broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to heal; or there can be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatment is, when there is no wound with the break, to have two assistants: one should hold the shoulder where the collarbone is broken; and the other should stretch the neck towards the affected side. Then, with your fingers, adjust the break so that it is aligned and there is no sign or evidence of the break.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place a round pillow made of cloth or wool under the shoulder of the patient; and they should relax the collarbone, and you should hold the pillow in your hand, adjusting the break so that it is aligned correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone out of its socket because it is too deep, then the patient should lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder, and the assistants should push the shoulder upwards, so that the collarbone bone is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you find it broken, you should split it open; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any protruding piece, cut it off with one of the knives you have; but place the tool under the forceps to direct the syrup.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It should be the size of a spoon, and not too thick, as wide as it needs to be according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; and it must have two heads, as you can see, one wide and the other narrow, according to the shape of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the opening is small, or if you doubt there is a hot abscess, pack the wound with bandages and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot absesses come, wet a bandage in rosemary oil and garlic and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or cut, is to place on the bone the plaster made from mill-powder and egg white, and put light sponges on top, and if necessary, place a spear underneath the splint; then take a very wide band of about 5 inches, and place a folded piece of cloth on top of the sponges and plaster; then take a thin staff of 3 fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the band so that the ends of the band hang down; and place the staff over the fracture, and turn the band up over the neck, and under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the affected shoulder blade; and tighten it from each side, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture in alignment, and you clearly see that the staff does not move over the broken bone, then adjust it every day, and when the ligature eases, tighten it again; and have the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, place a small pillow under the shoulder blade to raise the shoulder; this will ease the dislocation of the collarbone through the stretching of the shoulder, or you can bind the arm to the neck and not release it in case of any adverse events for up to 20 days; then start the plaster again if you see that it is needed, and tighten it and leave it like that until it is healed; it is usually healed within 28 days, but some people heal faster.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then the shoulder breaks or widens in the middle, and one feels it only by touch; then adjust the apparatus according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then put powdered flour on the wound with a lot of egg, and light gauzes, and place a double drape on top; then place a large, thin board on top, a little wider than the shoulder, and if there is any hair under the board on the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen gauzes so that the board lies evenly; then tie it tightly with a large bandage so that the board does not move from its place, and check the ligature every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it, and adjust the board if it has moved, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is complete, loosen it, and be careful, for it is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out above, and not under the heart, then split it open, and the bone, and do as we have said in the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe an abscess with heat.Et se li os est brise, et point tent avant, si met sor le leu de la brisure, un poultice d’uef et de molin, si que li espaule soit frouide; et remettet sor la brisure, un poultice d’uef et de lin, et estoupes legieres, et l’estraint a grant bende.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break in the stone
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The penis is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the foreskin.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks strength, and feels numb, and perhaps vomits blood, and the hair falls out from the broken bone, and he feels no feeling in it.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a pillow between his shoulders, then press his shoulders together and bring the ribs closer together with his hands, making sure the bone is positioned correctly; then apply poultices and bandages over the fracture site, using a light pressure, and wrap it in a cloth, tying it so that it does not move; then wind the bandage around the waist tightly and comfortably, checking every hour to see if it needs tightening; and if there is corrosion or itching or pain or an abscess at the site, quickly remove the bandages and poultices and treat the area as needed; then re-apply the poultice and bandages, tightening them until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	You should know that broken ribs only occur on the large ones in the back and in the chest, and they only bend because they are slippery; this can be discovered through examination of the two areas.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the break even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a bandage, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the broken ribs are bent downward, the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; they also have a cough and vomit a large amount of blood, which is a serious illness, and the elders have given it great concern.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly, in order to push the broken ribs outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not believe that hot abscesses will come to life unless they have first died down.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should put cupping glasses over the area to draw out the excess fluids, and this seems reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cupping glass will draw out the vital fluids due to the weakness of the body.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with soft wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to apply even pressure all around, then it should be treated with a poultice of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that protrudes through the skin, and there is doubt about the patient, then one should split above the location of the broken rib, and place an instrument underneath to protect the lung; and then one must cut the bone, and gently pull it, and then sew the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful abscesses arise, place moistened cloths in rose oil and apply them to the affected area; and treat the area around the abscess as needed, and let the patient lie quietly on his side where it is, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it can be bent; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will recover or not, take note if his hands are soft and swollen and dead-looking, and he cannot move them or straighten them out, and when you prick him with a needle, he doesn't feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that in many cases it is fatal; and if he can move them and feels the pain when they are manipulated and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the illness will be cured if proper treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition arises in the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will recover or not, pay attention if his feet are swollen, and if the symptoms are present in his hands, and there is flatulence and urination against his will; and when he lies on his stomach, there is urination against his will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is sleeping on his back and he wants to turn over, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly; therefore do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, then the condition is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply a hot poultice to the spine if there is an abscess, and then apply one of the comforting and drying ointments, and bind it with a bandage; and instruct the patient to rest and not sleep on the painful part until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, you should cover it with a bandage; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat it with ointment as needed until it is healed; and if the shoulder-bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow," grab your left little finger with your right hand, and apply the poultice and bandage evenly, if you need to; then bind it tightly, and if there is a broken bone, splint it and remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It may happen that the bone of the hip is fractured, and if it does, there will be a slight lessening at the head; and it extends long and declines to the sides, and brings pain to the area, and puncturing, and swelling in the place that is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as far as you can reach the fracture; and know which is the fractured part and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the head, then put it back into place so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture extends long, or declines inward, then let the patient lie on his stomach, as far as the restoration of that fracture can be prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the plaster, and then put a splint of wood or of horn on top, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move; and treat the area beneath the rib cage until the color is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if swollen abscesses arise, do not touch them until the swollen abscesses are resolved, and apply what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and treat it as appropriate, if there is no bad development; and that is the way to do it.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of two methods. The first method is to take a wooden staff of average thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Tie the two ends of a rope to the staff, and pull them upward, and let the patient sit on a chair; then have the patient swing his broken arm over the staff until he feels pain in the shoulder, and put a curve in the staff, then stretch him downward while a helper holds him steady; then have the patient hold the break in place with both hands together, until the break is set as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to have the patient lean forward over his knees, and tie his hand to his neck; then have one minister hold the broken part in place with his hands, and the others pull on each end of the rope, stretching him apart.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, then tighten the ligature below the fracture, and above it, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you should put one ligature in the middle below the joint, and another towards the neck, under the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the neck, then a ligature should be placed lightly and without labor, so that the fracture is even on both sides; then adjust the fracture as it should be, and tighten it, if no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a deep abscess comes, do not drain it until the seventh day, and put soft linen in vinegar and rose oil on the abscess, so that the deep abscess is soothed; then drain it, and the way to drain it is to put the ointment on the break, then assemble the arm above the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the cloth, and drain above the shoulder, and above the arm, so that the arm is in place, if nothing moves it or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use a splint, and put a larger and stronger splint over the break, with an inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be large enough that it extends 3 inches beyond the break on each side; then drain over the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter, more strongly and less slowly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting and tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt an abscess, then leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the ligature every three days so that itching or swelling does not appear at the site, nor the swelling come to the member because it is too tight.Et se il est ains estrois k’il enfleure et prurite ad esgare, si le deslie un pouce ou deux sus la briseure, et le remets en son leu; et s’il n’est pas trop longement ligiez, il ne puet demorer, mes il velt et revint a son leu.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you treat it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, and the dislocation is not reduced within three days or more, let the patient sleep on his back, and place his hands on his stomach; and put beneath the shoulder a cushion filled with wool, evenly packed, and every hour of the day or night, observe that the broken limb does not move, nor become soft in its joints; then treat it with medicine, and give him food as we have already specified, so that the food reaches the innermost parts; and when he begins to recover, let him eat solid food.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to take 40 days to heal; and then one should reset them, and administer baths and ointments to ease the pain.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and swollen, it will take two or three months to heal.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius". The ulna is smaller and is located near the armpit, while the radius is larger and is situated below the small finger. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, sometimes only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small vessels are broken, their restoration and healing is easy; but when the large ones are broken, their healing is difficult, and they cause more grief than when they are all broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small vessel that is broken, then one must gently extend and adjust it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large vessel, then one must press harder; and he should lie on his back, with his arm raised above his head, and his hand lowered below the other fingers, and he should cross his legs over himself, and the pillow under his head to raise it so that he does not labor at all; then the attendant should extend his arm towards the affected side, either to the elbow or to the wrist, while another attendant holds the arm above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he places the bandages evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, place each one in its place, and if any stick in the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision through the skin and bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the fracture, I have spoken about it in the individual chapter; take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of this restoration abscesses occur, they must be glued over with cerotin made from rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and then the bandage is applied gently on top, until the hot abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerotin, and apply the plaster of mill-powder with egg white, and then the bandages, and let the bandage on the fracture be a bit stronger and wider than the others; and you should have six bandages on the arm in various positions: if the fracture is in one of the bones, or two; and tighten more over the fracture than anywhere else, lessening gradually as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages on the fracture be soft and moist, not hard or rough; and use a thread made of linen for tightening, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And examine the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wet the limb with warm water until those itches are soothed; and let the limb not be pressed or restricted to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the stretching, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones displaced, address it similarly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you perceive that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little and leave it like that for some days, until the nourishment reaches it; and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have described happen to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or inquire within, then let him put his hands around his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and convulsion, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, according to the combinations and complexes of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, one should make the patient's arm straight, and have him extend his hand and straighten the broken bones as much as possible; then he should place an emetic on the skin, and if there is no abscess, then he should apply a poultice. Then the patient should rest for 24 hours in a comfortable position, with the affected area elevated above the heart, and keep the wound clean and dry to prevent infection.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the stomach of the plant, make a sphere of fabrics, and instruct the patient to hold it against their broken plant; then stretch it with a long strip of fabric, and hold the cloth in place with a hot candle as big as the palm of your hand, stretching it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the outside, you should place one cloth on top and another underneath the plant, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is on one of the fingers, if it's the thumb, set it straight as needed and hold it in place; and if the fracture is on another finger, like the index finger or another, straighten it and bind it to the adjacent healthy finger; or you can bind them all together, whichever is easier, or you can place a cloth on top, like a poultice; take care with the restoration and treatment of a hot abscess, and dry up any fluid that arises, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see this when they move forward and backward; their restoration is by binding one above the fracture and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each assistant stretches their band to their side equally; and this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, one of the ligatures should be towards the buttock, and the other ligature below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then the ligature should be on the side of the knee, and the extension should be below; then put the mirror so that the bone is equal to its natural shape with his two hands, until it is straight according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, unless an abscess comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside and then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is done in the following way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap a hard double folded bandage around the fracture, and leave off the excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee on the side, and let the end of the thread come up above; then go back over the leg and thigh with the bandage, then put the splints over the fracture, and put one splint over the bone of the leg; then stretch the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the ligature equal, then begin to tie it tightly in 3 or 4 places over the fracture; and the more you go above the fracture, the less you tighten it; then feel both ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and tie 3 splints that are on top, then go back down to the foot at the end of the thread, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, until an abscess or swelling comes, or something similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if something happens there, then loosen it and address what is happening, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone sticking out, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the area should be split open and the wound cleaned, as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken in this way when splints are placed on it, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, with treatment made in this way, the patient is not healed.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you shall know that the leg is restored in one day or a little less or more, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groove of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, then there is only a split or perforation; and it happens to all injuries, whether with pain or not, and everyone feels it.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put it back in place with the fingers, as long as it can be; then apply the plaster, and if necessary, put on a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions; then treat each incident as needed until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by the right name "mustelz" and the other is called "foscile"; and all injuries happen as they do in the arm, and therefore its restoration is the same as that of the arm, and its operations are all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns upside down everywhere.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the small bones are broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain and sees it clearly; and it turns inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, bring about an extension, and make it even, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints that reach from the top of the leg to below the knee on either side; then wrap two bandages around them, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point the leg should not be able to bend to the right or left, and thus it is well; and some administer a wooden bar that extends from the top of the leg, and they place the leg upon it so as to prevent movement, and properly they apply it at the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day to check for any hot abscesses or other accidents; and treat until healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the foot there can be a fracture and in both feet, and there is only bruise in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the leg bone is broken and you see the bones protruding above each other, then have the patient lie on his back as if he were walking, and then place your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, and then press down until they return to their places; then apply the ointment and bandages, and put a small, flat stone under the arch of the foot, and then bind it firmly in place with bandages and other materials as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, treat them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the toe, making it slightly larger, and place under the foot the stone that I have described, and bind it firmly in place; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the stone underneath the foot; and let the top of the stone press firmly against the sole of the foot.
