Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have already discussed; and treat each case as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman's nature are broken, make her sit with her legs apart, then tilt her to the side towards her back, and have the wound filled with cotton, and place a stone the size of an egg inside; then help the woman stand up, and gently press her back little by little, and then the cotton will come out as it enters the nature, and the bone will return with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days: the fracture will be restored. Then take a sheep's bladder, tie a cane to the opening, fill the entire bladder inside the nature; then blow into the cane firmly, until the bladder is inflated within: the nature will return the fracture; then have it filled with cotton, and leave it like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the man's or woman's finger is broken, treat it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from him who devotes himself to studying and understanding my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks show in many ways the right way to restore them; understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For a broken penis, take a goose's gullet and insert the penis into it; then wrap a cloth around it and leave it for three days, checking on it occasionally, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, or similar, to be bled immediately, in accordance with the bleeding we have described earlier.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then remove the vitriol, if you don't have anything else, and then start to reset the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if no abscesses appear.Et si la brisure est en jointe de corps, ou il n’y a pas de plaie, s’il le peut demourer ains que il n’y ait pas de contusion ou de lesion, qu’il demoure assiez sans se muevre, si com nos avons dit avant.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the fracture is in a joint of the body, or there is no wound, if it can remain without movement causing contusion or injury, it should remain seated and still as we have said before. And if abscesses appear, then leave the reset until the next day, as long as the abscesses are soothed, and don't touch them on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about a bad accident.Et si li membres sont contuziez ou les os briziez, et qu’il ne demourent pas adés, si covient que tu remettes le membre a son leu, et le repos par tuit le jor, et la nuit, et la matinee, et par tuit l’endit qu’il doit demourer asez.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is apparent on the uncovered heart, then you must gently put it in place with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent to you to make it equal with your hands, then reset it with this instrument which is made of iron and is seven or eight inches long, and the width is according to the amount of the injury; and for this reason, it is necessary for the surgeon to press into the wound three or four times, according to what he needs in each case of broken bone; and let it be round and somewhat thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb while you are working, and let it be pointed at the end, and thick from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called «palainche», because the curved head of the bone should be placed on top of the visible bone; and it is bound in place once, so that it may return to its original position and be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot grip the bone well, then you must cut off the head of the bone so that the instrument can grasp it firmly.Et se li brisure sunt en un os qui ne se puet bien appercevoir, si covient que tu l’enleves adessable, si com il tuit est, et si le retournes a son leu.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incision or a saw, according to your ability; then take out what remains in the bone of splintered pieces and small fragments.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, you will know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Then have it so that it is in its place, then soak the cloth in red wine, and use it to clean the wound if it is dirty; and do not put any ointment or other substance on the wound that would cause pus and corruption to form; then administer bandages after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover all around it according to the size of the wound; and take great care so that the wound is not constricted by the binding. And many a fool has done this and caused death or gangrene in the patient; and the constriction should be looser than for other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is large or deep, and you doubt that a bad accident will occur as we have said, and you feel pain in the area, then bandages should not be put on it; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard rags, and tie them tightly.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days swelling around the wound, then remove what you have put on top and apply healing ointment to wounds, such as four-drug ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you should loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and closed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And one must prepare the limbs in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they persist for many days, and it cannot heal but keeps dislocating the bowstring, know that there are tiny pieces of bone causing this, so you must probe the wound with a needle, and remove all the broken pieces causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or other form of corruption occurs, then you must treat it according to what he said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bone, and similar large bones, do not treat it at all, for many die from it, but leave it to heal over twenty or thirty days; then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come upon the healing
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	There are many times after the healing of a fracture, especially when it is near a joint, that an ugly sight appears in the member; and by chance the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then that the patient is free of moisture: if the medic gives astringent remedies such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla and similar, so that you grind one or all of these substances together and mix them with wine, vinegar, egg white, or garlic; and put it on the night-time as poultices, and hold it firmly in place and do not remove it for several days; then remove it and start again until the swelling is gone. Or press it onto a well-made piece of plaster; for the property of plaster is that it removes all swellings from the limbs; if the swelling has become as hard as stone, and there is a need to remove it, cut into it, and make the excess apparent; or have it cut by some surgeon so that it is removed and healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one is that it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the limb could not receive nourishment; or due to excessive swelling; or due to too much movement, and not at the right time; or because there is a lack of blood in the body, and so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you should make the patient eat and drink to soften his body so that blood multiplies within him; and give him a bath, and joy and relaxation; then apply pitch to the affected member, so that the pitch attracts it to itself greatly, and often wash it with warm water until the pitch is drawn out to the member and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	and the limb straightens after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is crooked after healing, and the broken bone opens, and the shape of the member is deformed, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function; yet one must not believe foolish people who say that the limb should be broken again completely anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great harm results, and sometimes death; nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are recent, one should wash them with warm water, or cook softening herbs such as marshmallow leaves, and roots, and mallow, and similar medicines that soften. And you make a soothing ointment, such as well-prepared diaquilon, and you take the mucilage of marshmallow, and confit it with goose fat or sesamen oil, and apply it as an ointment; or you take figs, and grind them with colon fodder, and similar medicines that soften.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the dislocation is caused by continuous and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you must move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the crookedness is awoken and hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then one must cut it to the bone with a subtle incision; and apply poultice and care in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, one must now reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place will swell, and if one tries to reset it, one might do so with pain; therefore one should not move it when it is swollen: many times this brings on spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then let him rest until the abscesses are drained; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as the healing comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Then the jaws become dislocated and the dislocations of both are in two ways: they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are entirely dislocated and hang down towards the feet, and saliva flows from the mouth which he cannot hold back, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is enveloped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you should reset it quickly without delay; and in such a way that the minister grabs the head of the patient, and blocks his nostrils with one of his fingers at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and let the other two fingers be free, to press evenly; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And she looks at it equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is stuck, especially if both jaws are together, then they should be soaked in warm water and oil, so that they are gently reset; do not pull hard on the jaw, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back to the same position, and the mouth of the patient is closed well without softening, then place it on wet sheets with a cerote made of rose oil and wax, and then lightly bind it with soft bonds; and let the patient sleep on his back, and let his head be between two cushions, so that he does not move it to the right or left, nor does he exert himself to chew, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaw is bound and healed. Then he can eat whatever he wants lightly, and does not strain himself to open his mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset in an hour and are not converted to their place, then come fever and usual sickness, and perhaps intestinal distress, and perhaps vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is deadly; and many die from it within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceless cannot dislodge from the ribs within its continuance of the armpit, and it is dislodged sometimes to the outside, and they feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and stretches out his arms; then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return to its place; then apply the ointment and bandage it, and tie it; and the shoulder joint which is towards the neck cannot be dislocated; if it is, and it dislocates again at any time, reset it in its place as we have said; then apply the ointment and bandage, and tie it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus also is the shoulder joint returned when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way is that it dislocates at the part of the armpit below; the second is at the part of the foot; and occasionally it dislocates at the part above, and this happens rarely; it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates below towards the armpit, especially in those who are thin, for in them it is forced out; but in those who are plump, it pops out and goes back in smoothly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they get a concussion or a fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must test it until you are certain of its effectiveness; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you can identify a dislocation when it is down towards the armpit, and you will see a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear distinction between them; and you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and under the armpit at the top of the shoulder, just as if there were an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will see it clearly at the touch; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the hand of the sick person up high, then places his fingers under the shoulder blade, and raises the joint with force to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upward, then lowers it; and it will come back into place quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and they should be given soothing and softening ointments, such as a decoction of altis, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and they should be rubbed down; then the patient should lie on their back, and a thin mattress placed underneath them, neither too soft nor too firm, then place the pillow under their heel, and lift the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the affected side; while another minister holds the head of the affected side so it does not move downward; this shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it is not returning, do it according to this manner: and have a man present who is larger than the patient; he should stand straight toward the armpit, and push the shoulder underneath the arm of the patient, and lift the arm up so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the affected side downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, one can add some weight to him, and the dislocation will return right away.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one can also reset it in another way: one should insert a long stick into the ground, so that the shoulder is as straight as a pencil, neither too thick nor too thin; then it should be placed under the patient, but with a soft cloth over it, and the patient should be standing upright; then his hand should be stretched out below on the other side, and the joint will return to its place suddenly; and if it does not return due to all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a stick two arms long and four digits wide, which has a pointed end to go deep under the shoulder, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a soft cloth to the end of the stick so that the stick does not hurt the patient, then place it under the joint of the patient; stretch out his arm along the length of the stick, and tie the shoulder to the stick, and the arm to the head of the stick; then place the arm on top of a pillow, and stretch out the hand below, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way it is, you should then place a woolen sphere under the joint, then apply the prepared plaster made from mill dust, incense, and egg white, all over the shoulder and around it; then tighten it under the joint gradually, and tie the string onto the plaster, and hold the hand to his chest, and let the hand remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And he must eat little, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of place due to moisture that it has acquired, or for any other reason, then you should administer cautery at three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it still dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and he cannot lift his arm upwards, then you should know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are torn or stretched or relaxed; and you should know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation that is towards the bottom, and the breasts, or behind, is done by pushing and stretching with the hands, and one should treat it in the same way until it is healed.And if there is dislocation of the jaw, one should not let the patient eat anything hard for as long as the joint is uncomfortable, so that it can heal quickly; and then he can eat more after five or seven days, and move his jaw; and if it is stiff and not softened, it will be healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, there is pain in the limb, and with movement, the patient suffers many times, until that pain is relieved and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated by pins, and it returns with pins; and if it is dislocated everywhere, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one sees and feels it well, and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked and cannot bend its arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it so that the abscesses heal, for if the abscesses heal, then it will be painful to reset; and by chance it may not be able to be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and death may result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend its hand with your two hands; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands bent according to the elbow, around and underneath, and push the joint into its socket at its wrist, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when he bends his hand towards his hand, and strain at the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then it must be forcefully extended; and there are two ministers who extend the arm, and two others who hold it so that it does not move during extension; then the arm is bent on each side after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it; and when the minister has joined the joint with his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then closes the joint firmly, as much as possible; and when it is in place, he applies a dry poultice with egg white, then tightly binds the arm to the neck of the sick person, and leaves it for several days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not healing well, then reapply the poultice and the bandage, and leave it for some days until it is firmly in place; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is moved back into place and it still hurts, then bathe and rub it gently, and press until it is soothed; or put a poultice of fat mutton on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times until he is healed; and if you see that, put moist cow dung heated with butter on top, and press it on; then it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is healed, and its return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place gently, in the same hour that it was dislocated, so that the joint swells or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And for the movement, put the sick hand on a table, and extend the fingers, and look at putting it in an even position, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and bend it until it returns to its natural state; however, you must also check if it is in the right place; then put the sick person's backhand on a table and extend it and move it.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then let the patient lie with his back to his hand on the table, and the assistant places his hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it goes back into place now, that is good. If not, then strain it with soothing poultices on abscesses, and leave it like that without re-enunciating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then let the joint stay crooked; and do not hurt the patient more than when his hand is weakened, and he cannot hold anything: then know that the nerves are cut, or an artery; there is no other remedy except straining by cautery near the spot, and perhaps nothing else helps.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then hold it and leave it for .v. days, then loosen and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then wet it with warm water and rub it until it heals.Et s’il adons li viens de l’engien qui li i a en la maint, si le frote aigue chaude et li met sus l’emplaustre susdiz.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the bones of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the inside; then they are bent, and you put the dislocation in your pouch until it goes back into place, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for two days, and then put it straight that day; and do not bind it, as we have said, and loosen it at night, and make it move, and bind it again at night; and do this often, until it is healed. And do the same, if it is dislocated on the inside of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed. And do the same if it is dislocated in another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or collarbone is dislocated, there is no remedy, for death hastens the malady.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the egestions escape without voluntary effort, and he cannot hold them in, and many times a limb becomes paralyzed, either both thighs or both arms or one; and often the shin mutates into four parts; that which occurs at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is to find out whether the gilbositez occurred in childhood; if not, there is no cure nor salvation from it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which occurs from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient ways of cure described at great length, but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding, and have devised instruments in diverse ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes to the toe in front, there is no healing; and also that which occurs directly on both sides, and one cannot cure it without that which comes properly to the back, as I said; and it happens that the patient stretches his face in one place evenly, and has an extension underneath him so that he does not bend; then insert a stake at the head into the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a string under the seat of the dislocation, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two attendants hold the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the stakes; and they are well tied, the stake as we have said, and the physician places his palms on the spine firmly, until it is healed.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a table three yards long, and lie under the wall, and let the patient be on their side, and place the end of the table under the wall, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and let the patient put their feet on the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that, do it in the turn that turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should nail two torches to the end of the patient's arm, and two others by their feet, and have between each torch, above and below, a palm's width of space in length; and have in each torch an opening where the rope runs through, and the torches are firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of torches there is a turning torch, over which the ropes turn, and on the two turning torches there are two small torches a palm in length for turning the pulley; and then tie the rope that is among the pulleys to the pulley toward the head, and the other rope to the other pulley, and each of the ministers turns their pulley to all the rope, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, then apply a desiccant poultice with plenty of egg white, and then the tow, and then the tile of a three-foot-long board, which purples the area of the hunchback and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use the patient for subtle cooling until he is healed; and if anything comes in the end of health, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines, with the tile that we mentioned earlier; and sometimes they administer a piece of lead, and sometimes the appearance comes on the back spine, and one thinks it is dislocation; and it is the bone that protrudes, so one must not have presumption: it might bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You know that in the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only dislocations occur, not as in other joints; and the hip joint is divided into four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and most inside, and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, the diseased one is longer and the diseased knee more prominent than the healthy one, and the diseased one cannot bend its knee towards the fire; and the area which is nearby is swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the thigh bone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those to whom it comes from the inside, it is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those who get it from the front are that their leg is well according to its condition; nevertheless, they cannot bend their knee without pain, and if they want to walk, they cannot go forward, and they retain their urine, and the anger swells, and when they walk, they pass over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one whom it happens to in the back, is that he cannot spread his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this type of dislocation are that you examine whether the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its condition, and there is no treatment; and he must not be presumptuous.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one who has a fresh dislocation, and it is of the four types of dislocation, you should quickly turn the joint, and stretch it in and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.Et si ne revenra pas, sache que c’est des  .iiij. manieres de dislocations; et si est qu’il demoure au leu selonc sa disposition, si covient qu’il ait cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then you must prepare a strong minister, and stretch the leg very hard with two hands, or with a strap tied above the knee; and another minister stretches his hand above in such a way that he presses his hands under his heels, then tie him with a strong strap above the thigh; and another holds the head with a strap; and they all pull up and down at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once and remains dangling.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This stretching manner is common to all four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must apply pressure to the affected side. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, you should support the patient on his healthy side, then place the strap over the root of the thigh, and over the part below the armpit; then tighten the strap towards the armpit and towards the elbow. Then another minister should grab the patient's arms and squeeze the fleshy part of the thigh, and stretch it forcefully: the joint will return to its place immediately. This type of dislocation is the easiest to treat.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot reduce it in the manner we have described, then you must tie the patient's two feet together with a strong woolen cord around the ankles and knees, and the affected leg should be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him be hung from the end of a pole, with his arms outstretched above him about a length of an arm; then command a minister to hold the top of the thigh, and another minister who hangs with the patient to hold the thigh firmly, for the joint will now quickly return to its place.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is reduced, let the patient lie as we have described in the case of sciatica, and loosen the ligature on the affected leg, and also on the buttock; then place two hot coals, one at the head and one at the foot, and place a hot coal between the buttocks of the patient; and have a pile of moist cloths ready, so that he does not burn himself, then extend each minister towards him, and the surgeon must apply pressure on the dislocation with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it goes back, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the table and press him as we have said in the section on dislocations, and lay the patient on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, then one should stretch the affected leg gently, and according to what I have said; and place his weight upon the sore joint, then press with the other hand, and the leg will move downward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the hip, one must not stretch the patient downward or raise him up, but he should be positioned as if his hip were dislocated on one side, just as we described for lying on both hips; and he should lie on his face, with the leg stretched out as we said before, and someone should press down on the joint while he is on the table; and when the patient extends his legs and they are even, then adjust the thighs, apply the plaster, and restrain it with a bandage so that the hip doesn't move; and let him rest for three or four days, then loosen the bandage and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are even, then restrain it as before and leave it for three days; then loosen the bandage and let him walk comfortably until his limbs are strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of a dislocated knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in 3 ways: that is to know, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not straighten at the thigh, then you know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and put your back on their face, and put their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee firmly; and another minister extends their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it straightens its leg at the thigh easily; and put the plaster on, and let the leg air-dry at the thigh, and bind them together tightly for three or four days, then release it; and the patient should not exert themselves in walking until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not at all, then administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	Heels are sometimes split, and sometimes fully dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it hurts when touched in the affected area; the movements are light, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely healed, you should make the patient sit up straight, and hold his leg firmly by the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and gently pull the foot upwards; do this twice as we have said, by bending and pulling the foot; if it goes back into place, that is good; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will go back in; and if it cannot be reduced in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and fix the strap firmly in the ground between his buttocks, and wind cloth around it so that it does not slide; then one person holds the leg firmly, and another stretches the foot upwards with their hands or with a rope tied to the ankle; then stretch each person equally, and have the strap held tightly between the patient's buttocks to hold him in place as he is stretched; then put your fingers over the dislocation, and another person pulls on the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will quickly go back into place.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at its worst, then put the plaster and bandages on, and tighten it firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and be careful of the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature loosens, then tighten it again; then untie it after a third or fourth day, and let the patient walk after four days; and if he walks before that time, there is no guarantee that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	and if it comes from fever or from a cold, or from a disease of the bed, or from a disease of the litter, you treat him in the manner that we have said;
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, they must be carefully extended without effort, and this is an easy matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the foot, you should make the patient sit on a flat surface or a table that is completely level, and put your foot on what is exposed of the joints, then press your foot firmly, until it goes back into place; and when it is even again, and nothing is exposed, put a two-legged board under the sole of the foot, then tighten it firmly, and leave it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure unless you are wise in the art and have used it for a long time, and unless you are compassionate and merciful and slow to anger; and at the beginning use things that soothe hot abscesses, and leave the patient in the hand of God if you do not see hope of healing; and when you see hope, then immediately move the limb back into place so that the hot abscesses heal; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing hot abscess remedies, and treat the wound as it should be done with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture and broken bones, set the bones and do what we have said for simple diseases; and beware of falling into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will bring change according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	So be it.
